Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it "cure contuse", and you must make the patient who has this illness to have hair on his forehead; then you make III cuts on the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the cuts be as II do across the forehead going down until the nose, and the other two are at the sides above the temples, and beware of cutting the arteries that are at both sides above the temples; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles; and each wound should be a width of III doigts across; then have ready a piece of sponge and much cloth to wipe the blood, then apply the spatula sharp on both sides as this figure shows:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is above the temple until the second incision; and scrape all the skin that is between the two cuts to the surface of the skull bone, then do likewise from the middle incision until the other second incision, and then remove this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert into the first groove the instrument called "cultellaire," and it is very well cutting on one side, and on the other side is smooth, not cutting, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge towards the flesh of the heart, and the smooth side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle groove.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to where it opens into the heart, and then make another incision in the middle groove up to the other side; and then extract blood evenly, and apply pressure to stop bleeding; then place a pad of old cotton in each groove, and cover with cloths moistened in wine and oil and rosemary, and guard against abscesses forming; and on the third day loosen the bandage, and bring large poultices of vinegar water, then treat with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the rheum of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When cataracts come frequently to someone, and you see the eyes swollen and small, with weakened vision, and the membranes burned; and the hair falls out, and in the head there is severe pain like ague, and the patient sneezes; then you know by these symptoms that those matters and that catarrh do not come from anything but many veins, and the mucus that is there indicates this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient behind their forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another at the top.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And start from the incision at the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go until it reaches the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when chewing; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate between the two edges of the incision and put old cotton there, and bandage with linen; then wrap with moistened cloths in wine and oil, and guard against hot abscesses; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat with substances that stimulate growth.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In such a manner: take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make an ointment; and apply it to these wounds to promote flesh growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the obstruction of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains, animals, or stones from mines or similar objects such as iron; seeds, such as peas, beans, and lentils; or flowing substances such as water and pus and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or other object falls into the ear that does not fit in the ear and does not grow in the ear, place the ear towards the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then let a few drops of violet oil or cumin oil be applied, then proceed with extraction; and make them sneeze from powdered substances, and plug their nostrils when they are about to sneeze, and place around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and hold the ear up.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often the stone comes out through this treatment; and if it does not come out, treat the extraction with fine forceps, which are described here:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the forceps, that is good; if not, then use a fine hook made of small double wire; and if it does not come out even by this method, make a thread of silk and insert one end of the thread through the ear canal firmly, and plug the area around the thread with soft wax so that air cannot enter along the thread; then pull it out forcefully, for often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in such a manner, take birdlime from which birds are caught, and place some instrument that fits properly on it, and wrap a bit of cotton around it; then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she cannot escape from all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear as for an abscess to come out and spasm; and the manner of cutting is that you make the patient bleed from the cephalic vein, and extract blood according to the measure of her strength, then sit the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where it hangs down; and let the cut be as a crescent until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck hastenly with your mouth; and treat until she is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if the grain is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer this subtle plaster according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision of that swelling.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the swelling is moist due to moisture from the ear, until you have done many cases; then extract it with fine forceps and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the acute condition when it falls into the ear, the patient should use sneezing powders first, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on that same side where the ailment is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it comes out because of that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If that is not the case, take many stones according to the length of your thumb and light ones, and heat them slightly in the fire; then place one stone in the patient's ear, and have him stand on it with one foot from the other side, and hit the stone in the ear with another stone; and do not stop hitting stone upon stone until all the water comes out, and thus will all come out; and if you wish, take a reed, and put one end of it in the ear, and burn the other end with fire until the softer part of the reed is burned; then repeat with another reed until all the water has drained out, as we have said about the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of the creature, if it is small in size, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, then use tweezers for extraction; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in treating distillations, and if the treatment does not help, then you must look at the ear in the sun: if any worms are visible, remove them with fine forceps, and if none appear, take the following remedy:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And make it narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the finer end of the remedy into the ear according to the severity of the patient's pain, then gradually form it all along the length of the remedy; do this frequently until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out willingly, plug around the remedy with cotton as I have said for stones; and if they do not emerge as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have tested for worm removal, which you will find in the treatment of distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, as shown in its form:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be of silver or brass narrow through small holes, and above cover for dripping; and to press within the distillation with an instrument of brass well made for this, and if you want take a razor and wrap around the tip appropriately cotton; then pour your oil or your juice, and what you wish of your medicines in the tube, and the tube be in the ear; then put inside the razor all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled at the bottom of the ear; and let the patient feel it within, and let the distillation be a little heated over the fire as one distills into the ear; and guard that it not be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the congestion of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	Some children are born without any hole in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to a blockage of an injury or flesh inside the ear, and these obstructions sometimes occur completely inside the ear so that one cannot see it; and at other times there is a slight opening of the hole, and then one can clearly see it.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The one that is completely inside and cannot be seen requires difficult treatment in many cases, and when it can be seen, you should place the patient's ear in the sun; and look inside: if you see clear secretion, then proceed with this spatumile of which here is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting in front and completely flat at the back so that it does not injure the ear; if the secretion is flesh from inside the ear or the body of the ear, hold it with fine forceps and gently scrape it off until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if there is an obstruction in the ear, take a fine, light rasor and heat it slightly over fire, then place it in the flesh of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the obstruction causing pain in the ear, pierce it gently, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place a wick in the ear according to the width of the opening, and soak it in Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for as many days as it takes for the wound to heal, or take a wick and soak it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on it; and if you see that the ear is swollen, then you must extract the wick and replace it with another soaked in cerate made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling subsides; then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and cloths in cold water, and place them on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the bleeding which are in the treatment of hemorrhages.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althæna that comes from the eyes when they are moist and dry, you must stretch them with pliers and forceps, and cut a piece from its root with a scalpel; then place crushed vitriol over the area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they do not peel off, cauterize them with the lentil cautery and then incise after it has healed; and many times they need repair, as some part remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hailstones
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times things come out of the eyes that resemble hailstones in form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hail," and it is a collection of thick moisture above and below the membrane; the treatment is as follows: check if the hail moves from side to side, and it is easy to know; then cut it wide, then lightly peel each part, then grasp it with forceps, and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing a bit of the membrane, do not cause any harm to the patient; and if the incision is large, sew it up with a stitch, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, make no force, for the ointment will heal it quickly and regenerate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granule is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn the membrane over, and extract the granule with forceps, and cut and squeeze it from both sides; and if the membrane is separated by an incision, this does not cause harm; and when the granule is removed, lift the eye with salt water, and treat the area that regenerates flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the grease of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is generated in the membranes above the pupils, and this happens more often to children than to some people, and it greatly troubles their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason they lie down on their faces immediately, and sleep like that, and their membranes below their eyebrows are moistened with exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press that place with your thumb and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of work is that the patient places his head on your hand; then take a piece of linen and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach in each part, then place it over him; and press with your thumbs from both sides so that the exinach is assembled within the circle; then cut an incision through the moisture with a sharp spatula about as wide as the opening made for venesection; and cut the membrane perfectly until you reach the exinach; and in many cases, the exinach comes out of the incision, resembling a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull it then in one piece of torn cloth between your two hands to spread it out, and move your hand right and left until it is dispersed; and be careful not to add anything to the incision, so that you do not bring all the spatumile up to the eye, so that you do not injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the excrement does not appear at the beginning of the incision, enlarge the incision slightly until it appears; then pull it out as we have said, then moisten cloths in warm water and place them on the spot, and pull out bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are such people who grind salt and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he comes to the place of an abscess, treat with poultices alleviating until he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the eyebrows
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on the eyelids that are not natural, and they become inflamed, they harm the eyes and cause conditions such as habitual tears and inflammation of the eyelids and conjunctiva, to the point where it is a cause of eye destruction; and the treatment follows four methods: either by cautery with fire together, or by medicine according to what was mentioned before in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by canthi (eyelid edges), as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient in your hand, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, put a needle along all the thread; and let this be near the margin of the paper where the hair grows among these hairs, and draw the thread above all the paper, and turn it at the edge; then cut in the part below the paper, below the hairs attached, to all the stroma cutting from the large lachrymal gland up to the small one; then extract the thread, and put below the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth, then sign on the paper a figure of incision, like the leaf of myrtle, and always it must be that the figure is according to the quantity that you wish to raise the paper which is intended for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is need to cut a large quantity of the paper according to how the paper has softened; then make incisions all along the spatula on both lines that you have marked, and start from the larger tear until it becomes smaller; let one of the cuts be near the natural hair in the thickness of a root, then insert the needle into one of the two angles of the cut, and remove the skin entirely; then sew together the two edges with a single thread of fine linen, and wipe away the blood, and arrange any superfluous threads around both eyebrows with some sticky substances if you wish to do so; but if not, then do not worry about it, leave the suture and the threads until three or four days; then treat the wound without sutures with drying and binding agents because the paper lifts up suddenly from the wound and assembles itself, but the suture is cumbersome (as the ancients say), and these works are done without fear; and there is another way: which is to mark the paper in a shape similar to that of myrtle leaves, as we have described, at three inches apart according to the form shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut those which rise above the small forces evenly according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the parts are not even, take a needle with thread, and insert it in the figure; then place one thread beside the large wound margin, and the second thread beside the small one, and tie the two threads evenly together; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin where you have marked, as we have described, then stitch together the two edges of the wound by suturing, and heal it until it is healthy; and if an abscess comes from your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; but sometimes the hair on the paper turns: in such cases you should use what we have said about incisions; however, the stitching in both directions is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of the canthi is as follows: you should turn the paper and cut into it according to what I have said, then make two canthi by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatula is; and tie at the two ends where you hold the threads; then join one and the other gently over what protrudes from the paper of the eye, and pull the two canthi from the two parts firmly; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin which is pulled will die and become blackened and pus-filled until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, then cut it with force, and treat it until it is healed; and when the wound has closed, and if the paper has risen, and no more hair will grow there; and this is the form of the two canthi that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle and put in it a thin silk thread; then assemble the parts and tie one to the other finely, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then arrange in the socket another fine silk thread briefly, and knot the ends of the thread; then have the patient place his head in your hand; and let it be near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for this is a subtle and delicate work, then put the needle throughout the socket at the root of the hair adjacent to it, and make it pierce quickly onto the paper until you draw it over the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the socket, and insert into the socket that hair, if there be one or two or three or more; then pull your hand back so that the hairs come out fully on the socket with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair is treated and does not come out with it, draw the needle back along all the thread that you have inserted, until the hair comes out of the hole above and you can see it with your eye; then pull out the needle and leave a small piece of thread behind for two days or three, until the hair hardens in its place and flesh grows over it; and if the hair is short, accompany one long hair from the natural hairs, and lift it up along with that which you have left, until it is raised up and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the pus from the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or pus comes to the eye, there are two ways it can occur: one naturally, and the other unnaturally.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by sudden wound, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work is that you should cut open the wound, and separate its edges, and place linen strips inside it, and keep it until it heals; and you must not use in the treatment of it things that dry out and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness will return worse than before; but use things that soften it, such as fenugreek; and boil water with rue and flax seeds, and apply melted dairy fat mixed with some oil, and wrap a cloth around it, and treat it with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you must ensure it does not seal up according to its former shape; and all the works we have mentioned are nothing other than remedies for this disease, so that it does not return to its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is called "axacrati" in truth, and it has natural causes and accidents.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the method of treatment is that you take a needle, to which there should be double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and have it pierce from the left tear duct all the way to the right, so that the thread passes through two points of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above completely over the needle, and apply pressure with a spatula measuring one spatumile wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should, that is good; if not, take the scraper and place it in the crevice, and turn the paper, and make two cuts along the inside of the paper; and let the ends of these two cuts be at the two corners of the incision you have made, and form an angle so that when they are joined together, the shape is as that of a letter called "I griesche"; then remove the flesh according to the sharpness of its edges inside, from what is under the paper, then join the two parts separated, and sew them together with linen thread; then treat it with the cure we have spoken about for softening medicines, and tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a cut or seam or cautery, it is necessary that you make a full incision below the hairs of the paper, and as stated above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare remedies with all their power to bring back the figure to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what there is need for work and instruments in many situations.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the sudden swelling of the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling occurs to people in such a manner that the skin above is swollen with the white of the eye, and they cannot move or perform their natural actions, then you must insert the tip of a razor under the skin and lift it up; and stretch it with forceps, until you remove what is attached to the delicate membrane, which should not be too sharp or cutting, so that the patient cannot endure a razor that cuts the eye's delicate membrane too sharply; and make your incision, by which you peel off this assembly, gently, so that the skin returns to its natural form; and heal all of this assembly, and sometimes put salt water in the eye, and lift it with fresh water; then place between the skin and the eye a piece of linen cloth, and apply to the eye wool moistened abundantly with egg white; and after three days use poultices and soothing substances until they are healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail exists in two manners: one is nervous and similar to hard skin, and another which is not nervous, but is like white frozen moisture, such that when it is touched by iron and one thinks to remove it with pincers, it cannot be done; and both of these begin near the large tear duct, and grows little by little until it covers all of the sight and light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient places their head in your lap, then works their eyes; and lift the paper with your hand, then coil the nail with pincers gently, and stretch it above; then take a needle, and put horsehair, or goat hair, or oxhair on it, and strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and insert it into the nail, and pierce it completely with the needle, and tie the nail to a thread and stretch it above, and shave off all the hair from the side of the nail that is next to the tear duct and along the hair to the top, then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear duct with the subtle spatula and small forceps, and leave the natural flesh of the tear duct so that by the incision the flow of tears does not become accustomed; and sometimes the nail is stretched only on a clamp, and with thread, as we have said; then shave off all the subcutaneous tissue where this form is:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatumile does not touch the thin skin and break it, and that the pupil is not pierced; and after the incision throw into the eye a little bit of salt ground up, and from the collyrium made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then treat it with what is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not loose and you cannot insert a needle, and the hooks cannot enter, this kind of nail problem is often treated with many medicines; and it grows as I have described in the division, and if you wish to cut it, do so gently according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail gently above, and if you see that it is slightly reduced and the reason for it is pressing, then distill from your mouth into the eye collyrium made of litharge and red collyrium and ground salt, and plug the eye until the next day; then continue with the other work according to this same method until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If something is contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then treat it, and cure the hot abscess first until it is healed, then resume work as before, until it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid harms the eye with great damage, then suspend it to the ala nasi, and cut part of it but not all, so that no tears come from the wound; then drip into the eye red collyrium made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some eyes, red flesh sometimes grows and covers the pupil, restrains it to turn outward, and looks like a baluster rose; and the treatment is that the patient places their head in your lap, then work on the eyes, and roll all that flesh with suitable hooks, and hold it firm by force; then cut the first layer of flesh, and continue cutting until you reach the end, careful not to injure the eye during the operation; and let the incision be as described for nail excisions and minor surgeries as illustrated later in this chapter; when the incision is complete and all the flesh removed, apply a poultice made from ground seeds or other red collyria and similar corrosive medicines, then place cotton soaked in egg white over the eye to prevent a hot abscess; if anything remains and there's concern of a hot abscess developing, leave the eye alone and treat any abscess with soothing remedies for hot abscesses; continue your work until it is healed, and so on when flesh is similarly attached to the eye.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you must ensure that the treatment of each weak eye follows the natural course; and for accidents, use ironwork; and do not place your hand in any of these works until you see that this member can withstand the work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Veins are red and covered over the eye, and their work endures in vision and weaken the eye all day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, first you must examine whether the eye, in which the inflammation is present, is isolated, and there is no other disease except the inflammation; then treat it in this manner: instruct the patient to place his head on your hand, then suspend those veins along the entire vein according to your wisdom, and let the veins be fine double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two needles be in stages on the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then gently press on the veins with forceps and wipe the blood hour after hour until you see the veins withdraw from the eye; and be careful not to damage the eye with the tips of the forceps, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your work so as not to miss any veins; and when you have done this, drop collyrium of green and red color into the eye to dissolve what remains of the sore.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to collect all of this at that hour, apply a plaster over the eye made from soothing ingredients to relieve the pain of the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pain subsides and there is assurance of a warm abscess, then restart according to this manner as described above until he is healed; and this is the form of applying pressure:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The physician calls this type of fistula "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it does not heal, there is pus that must be incised where it should burst, and drain all the moisture that is inside, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, remove it with all the instruments that are shown here; it is called "aspre chief," and should be made of iron to fit the head roundly, and should have teeth like a file as shown in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place over the site of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand slightly until you know that the corruption is removed; do this several times, then restore the area with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the tissue is adhered and flesh grows there, and the body of the bowel is adhered, and it remains thus for forty days, and it does not renew itself and is not inflamed, and no bad incident occurs, then know that he is healthy; if this is not so, then there is another reason to bring the fistula back to the anus according to this form: which is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and by dry medicines, and when it becomes uncovered take one probe according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and the shaft should taper up to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the temple, and move your hand from the eye one inch, then turn the probe completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels this if he holds his hand on his anus; and afterwards restore the area with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when flesh grows and hardens the tissue, let the matter go to the anus; it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the outlet of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is fully open and there is no obstruction or decrease in vision, you must bind the patient; then heal it, then apply suction cups to suck without hitting, then place over the eye a plaster made of cedar, aloes, incense, and sarcocolle, and then extract the eye, and apply plasters with bandages and cloths; and the method for the cloths is that you take soft cloths and double each one into four, and then place them on top of each other according to how much the eye needs; then press it down tightly with a hard bandage, and restart the suction cups without hitting; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the plaster becomes loose, you must tighten it greatly; then remove the dressing after the day and night, and if you see the eye recovering, that is good; if not, continue applying plasters, cloths, bandages, and suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the tearing of a woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the woven cloth, then it is opened up, and something hard like resin grain appears beneath the skin, which is terrifying to see; then if you wish to repair it, work as if you were inserting a needle at the root of the affected part from below up to above, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the side; and pierce through, leaving the first needle according to its position; then cut out the area of the double thread and tie one part of the woven cloth around it tightly, then remove the needle and place wet wool soaked in plenty of egg over it; leave it until the thread falls off with the cloth, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by a circle of cloth from each side until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye appears inflamed, pierce it with a fine spatula that comes in perfectly straight from the eye, and draw out the watery humor and bring down the eyelid; then extract until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing more than an accumulation in the eye, resembling an inflow of water, but it is not actually an inflow; and the manner of its appearance is such that you should seat the patient on a properly prepared and straight chair, then take his head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the accumulation come up to your eyes; then let it remain there without descending and obscuring the light, and observe if the patient can see things as he usually does; and if it does not descend below as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Situate the patient between your hands, then take the spatula and make an incision on the corneous membrane, a little at a time along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneous membrane and the eyelid, until the blood comes out; and when it has come out, pour into the eye hot honey mixed with honey, or water boiled with fenugreek and honey, then treat it further as necessary until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	for the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have described the appearances of the waters in the division, and what is necessary for piercing them; act according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you sit the patient between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and press the healthy eye tightly with your fingers; then place the paper of the affected eye in your left hand if it is the left eye, or in your right hand if it is the right eye; then take in your right hand, if the eye is the left one, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if the eye is the right one; then place the tip of the instrument along the eyelid by the thickness of a thread at that white part of the eye near the lower tear duct, then insert the instrument called "almagda" forcefully, and turn your hand until it pierces into the white part of the eye, and feel when the almagda reaches an empty space; and the length of the path of the almagda should be as deep as the space from the inner corner to the end of the black part; this is the eyelid; you will see the bone on that paper by the clarity of the corneous membrane, then place the instrument until it reaches where the water is, and press out along one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water flows now, let the patient see before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting briefly, if the water rises again through the second path, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly placed and it does not rise further, gently extract it in small turns; then add a little powdered caraway seed to the water, and lift the eye from there.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place around the eye plugs made of wool soaked in rose oil and an abundance of egg white, and secure them with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply it mixed with an abundance of egg whites.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, because there are people who have eyes too hard, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", of which here is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but act carefully, then insert the almagda as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a sleeping chamber, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and be cautious of all movements, and give him light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his disposition until the third day; then release him in that same dark room and test his sight, showing him some objects, and then rebind him until the seventh day; and it is not necessary for you to do this during the time of treatment or immediately after the incision, but it is necessary to wait because the fluid rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If abscesses come that you must treat before the seventh day, refer to the eye of someone who specializes in reducing abscesses; and when it is eased, then release the sight and place a small bandage on it for some days, and keep it in a dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house little by little, and return to your normal activities; and know that no student should intervene in such a case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from Yrach who told us that in their country people use almagda for puncturing blisters, from which water is drawn, but still I have never seen such a thing in our land, nor have I read about it in ancient books; and perhaps it is a new practice.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of alum, for those who do not know them see; and they should be properly of brass:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the heads of these be of the same subtlety, and the rear in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes flesh on the nose grows in various ways, some of which seem like many-footed scorpions; and there are such cases where it has flesh raised with red color, and there is smooth skin of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In the case of that flesh which is smooth and not raised, you should seat the patient between your hands facing the sun; work his nostrils, apply the lancet to those parts, and cut them out; then continue as much as you can sustain with a fine sharp spatula until you know that all the flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be cut, then treat it with all the instruments finely and gently, so that nothing remains; and if without doing this the abscess breaks out, treat it as is appropriate; and if these are malignant abscesses, act quickly and cauterize until the blood stops flowing and all the flesh is removed, then apply a soft and clean dressing of vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the dressing works and moisture comes up to the throat, know that it is healing; and if the moisture does not come out properly as it should, know that there is new flesh on the bone above where the instrument cannot cut: then you must put a thick linen thread through it, tied loosely with spaces between each knot; and place the patient's finger in the thread at the opening of the nostril, and pull gently until it comes out through the mouth; and many times children in schools do this, and it is an easy thing for one who wants to do it; then hold one end which comes from the nose with one hand, and the other end which comes from the mouth with the other hand, and pull alternately while being careful of the knots in the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the root has corrupted the flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and place it back into the nose as before; do this for III days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of flesh; and then put a plug of some kind in the nose for several days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, on which oils and medicines are dripped into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it may be of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and the conduit should be similar; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and let the instruments be full for purging the head; and have I handle at the top to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh upon the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" is born on the head of the nose, and it grows and becomes large over time, to the point where it is visible upon looking at it; and for this reason you should cut it at the beginning, remove it entirely, then apply the cautery or hot medicine to its place; and if one delays cutting it until it is large, beware if it is hard, of fiery color, and has poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an entrenched abscess, for when you cut it even once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of a fiery color, and you see that all of it can be cut without fear, empty the patient and cut it sensibly, and treat the place with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is broken and sewn up
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solutions for continuity come to one of these cartilage works, there is little benefit, except in some men.
