Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when this happens to anyone, it is necessary to examine whether the wound is fresh and full of blood; then join the two lips into one seam, and treat until it heals; and if the two edges are separated from each other on both sides, you must scrape all parts of their core until they bleed, then bring together the two edges into one seam, and press them tightly, and apply powder made from dragon's blood and ground incense; and place the powders under a piece of adhesive or another sealing plaster, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of suturing is that you bring together the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the suturing of the abdomen; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In some people, there is a hard abscess in the lips, resembling grains of wheat, small and large; then you must turn the lips inside out, cut into each node, grasp it with forceps, and cut it in every part; then apply to the site after incising boiled vitriol, until the blood is congealed; and then wash the area with lye, and treat the wound with dry remedies until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often on the gums grows attached flesh that the ancients call "albulus"; you must hold it with forceps, cut it at its root, and let the blood or pus run freely; then put over the place vitriol ground up, or other powders that constrict and dry; if this flesh returns after cutting, which happens often, cut it a second time, and cauterize: it will not return after cautery; these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of dirtiness/discharge
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are scabs that assemble at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth become black and yellow and worm-eaten, until the corruption reaches the gum, and the tooth becomes foul-smelling; you must seat the patient in your lap with his head in your lap, and extract the teeth or scabs completely, so nothing remains; and thus do for the blackness and greenish hue, and the yellowness and other stains, until they are clean; if one removes what is necessary at the first session, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything completely; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments for extraction, according to what the work demonstrates, because the razors used to remove rotten parts from between the teeth are different from those used around them; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay pulling it as long as possible, for one must not do this; because it is a very high substance until there is no excuse for pulling it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is compelled to have it pulled, you must be certain of the tooth that needs to be extracted.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the patient suffers from pain and believes it to be in a healthy tooth, leading them to have a good tooth pulled; yet the pain does not depart by this action until the bad extraction is addressed, as we have seen this happen before with such patients. When you are certain of the painful tooth, you should scrape around the tooth thoroughly for about one span's width to protect the gum from all sides; then gently grip it with your fingers or use fine forceps in small increments until it is properly loosened, and firmly secure the forceps; place the patient’s head between your knees, holding it steady so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth straightforward without breaking it, and if it does not come out forcefully, take one of these instruments and insert it gently on each side, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perforated and damaged, it is necessary to fill it with cloths where the holes are; and if you extract it gently with forceps, do not break it in the process; and it is very important to work around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful that you do not break it, and leave a part behind, and return to the patient due to the mischief of the root greater pain than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful that you do not act as ignorant surgeons do, who due to their haste and boldness sometimes break the tissue, and do not follow what we have described; but instead bring about sometimes through carelessness serious illness from the roots that remain, or from the tissue they break, as often happens; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the area with wine or herb juice and salt; and if bleeding continues, which often occurs, fill the area with powdered vitriol; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments with which one moves the teeth first should have long points and thick handles, so that they do not double up when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick parts so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of well-forged iron, and they should be toothed to hold the teeth.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after extraction, it is necessary to place cotton soaked in butter on the site for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the gum becomes softened, then you can insert the pincers called "algefri," which resemble a bird's beak; and they should be made inside like a file, and this is their form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with these forceps, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root and place the instrument called "althali," which is a plane, here is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be firm and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out from this, it is good; if not, then help with all the instruments, of which the forms come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has two rails, here is its form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools which are mentioned earlier in the context of teeth, and of this instrument that resembles large forceps, here is its form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be such that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of bone exist; and also other instruments which are not mentioned; and the wise masters find their own instrument by themselves according to what their work and the disease show them, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument due to the diversity of cases, if one does not break the cartilage or other bones, it may rot, so seek the instruments that should be used as I have told you, and aid with gestures, about which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-fitting to hold the bone so it does not escape, but can be held and removed; then restore the place with medicines appropriate for this, and if there is rot in the bone and it is small, remove it with all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth does not appear according to its natural position in the body, and the form is ugly, especially in virgin women, then you must know if the tooth has grown after another tooth and is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or smoothed: then split it; and if it grows sideways next to a tooth, take this instrument whose shape is like a small beak, and let it be sharp steel at its tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut it bit by bit over several days due to the hardness of the tooth, and so as not to move the others, and if it appears that you can file it, then file it with a tool like this one:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the file used to make needles; and file the tooth bit by bit over several days lightly, so that it does not move until it breaks off; then smooth it at the end with any plane, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, you must file down its roughness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue nor impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth become loose, either due to percussion or falling, and the patient cannot press on what they chew without them becoming displaced, and you have treated them with restraining medicines but it is ineffective; then they must be restrained with a gold wire, for silver thread becomes green and rots, but gold never moves. And let the wire neither be too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you wish to align the teeth, take the wire and fold it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the wire ends between any loose teeth, whether there is one or more, carefully until you reach a healthy tooth on the other side; then continue covering until you return to where you started, and pull your hand subtly and cautiously so that nothing moves; and secure your thread at the root of the tooth so it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the teeth of the wire with pincers, and assemble them, and place them between the healthy tooth, and position it so that it does not bite the tongue; then leave it as tight as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the wire falls out, tighten it with another wire; thus it will remain and serve in this way for all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two bad ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, place another in its place, fresh for fresh, as we have said; and do not intervene with anyone who is not wise and skilled, and sometimes one makes the form of a tooth from a piece of whalebone, and places it where the deficiency is, and tightens it as we have said, and it remains and serves for such a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	There is a time when this ligament that comes from under the tongue exists by nature at birth; or due to an accident of a healed wound. The procedure is such that you work on the mouth of the patient and hold their head in your hand, lift up the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament widely until the tongue is separated from its base, and if there is hardness or a knot, which is from the healing of a wound, insert an uncine (a surgical instrument) and cut it broadly in that manner. And be careful that the incision is not too deep, for the artery lies underneath; and when you have finished, lift up with rose water and maidenhair, or cold water, then place under the tongue a pad of linen; and bandage the patient each night so that the wound may not heal prematurely.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding continues, apply powdered vitriol to the area; and if it affects the blood, cauterize with a lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it colored black or hard and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it declines to blanchor and there is moisture, apply lancing with a fine spatula, and free it from both sides; and if your work affects the blood, apply powdered vitriol until it subsides, then return to your work until you exhaust all force; then lift the area gently and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes in the throat there come lumps which are called "godath," and they are properly referred to as the two tonsils, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and if they are not healed, be careful: if these abscesses are hard with a little sensation and of dark color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, nor for bloodletting; but leave it until it turns black, and then you will separate it, as it would break by itself; and if it has a white color and the root is fine, prepare the instrument to cut, but first see if the abscess lies quietly and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit before the sun, and place his head in your sight, and open his mouth and grasp the tongue with your hands, and press it down with all the instrument, which is of this form; and let it be of silver or fine brass like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see an abscess, then take a lancet and insert it into the almond (gland), and pull out more than you can; and extract some matter with cloth, then cover it with the instrument, which is of this form, that resembles forceps; and yet their heads are curved, one end to another, and they are very sharp, and are made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, cut it with pincers, of which here is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be cutting on one side and naming on the other; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot water, and warm and soothing liquid, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with water containing cooked pomegranate rinds or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is congealed; then treat it until he is healthy; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two tonsils, so cut them as you would the two tonsils equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman who had an abscess born within her throat, which is to say the tonsillitis; and I found that her entire throat was nearly closed off, so that the woman could not breathe due to the blocked passage, and could neither eat nor drink, and she would have died if she remained in this state for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had risen so high that it had forced two fingers wide through the two openings of the anus.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hurried then and inserted a lancet into one, then I pulled it out forcefully and removed a large amount of pus; then I did the same in the other opening of the anus, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the lancet into the abscesses, and cut part of them away, and no more than a little blood came out; thus was unblocked the passage of the woman's throat, and she now began to drink water and then wine, and I did not stop cutting from this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again quickly, filling up what I had emptied, until it became very large; then I treated it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it remained without growing further; and I left these parts, and do not know what God did with them after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When rheum descends into the eye and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is detached, large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the swollen abscess has subsided, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and if it is round and assembled and is not long; and it is bloody or of dusky color or black, then you must avoid cutting it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it as I have said, according to its whiteness and length, you must seat the patient facing the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we made mention earlier; then insert a lancet into the eye, draw it out, and cut it with one of the two instruments that I mentioned for cutting the two glands.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut any flesh beyond the excess that is beyond the natural boundary; for if you cut more, it harms the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said about cutting the two glands, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of cutting, you must use cautery to calm their fearful senses.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of the cautery is sharp and potent.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient place their head in your lap, and then press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and confine it with sharp vinegar-soaked cloths so that they are not too thick or too clear; and apply this treatment with the following method and form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let there be on the head a bandage where one puts the medicine, as much as one spoonful, and place the instrument with all the medicine over the eye; and have the patient lying on their side, so that saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine, so it does not descend to the throat and close up; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it hardened and the twitching of the medicine is calmed; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and soak the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument with all the cotton under the eyelid, so that the cotton sticks to the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry after four or five days. And if you need to restart the cautery of the medicine, start again, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and have him rinse with cold water and gargle until he is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more valuable than incision or cautery; if it is treated by fumigation according to this manner, take chamomile and hyssop and origanum and rue and yarrow and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in one pot, and add salt, and boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and within the pot have an instrument covered as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or tin, and place one end in the mouth of the patient as the vapor rises up through the vein until the abscess is necrotized; after which repeat often until the abscess dries, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of a hot abscess's onset, for many things can happen; and do not perform this unless it is during the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a chain and place inside the head an egg white, so that the patient’s mouth does not get too hot; for the egg white does not let the vapor oppress the mouth, and this is both a good remedy and safe.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or thorn from fish, or something similar gets stuck in the throat. Therefore, you must extract what you can see and press on the tongue with all the instruments so that you can dislodge the object; and for whatever is not apparent and is lodged in the throat, it is necessary to induce vomiting in such a way that food cooked in the stomach is expelled; perhaps this will expel the foreign object. Or have the patient swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of wool, or a lettuce root, or dry bread; tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it; when it reaches the location where the obstruction is, it will adhere, and then you can pull out the object; if none of these methods work as we have described, take this instrument made of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head lifted up; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, nor push the bone inside; and move it gently as the patient pushes the instrument, so that it moves where the thing is loose; if pushed downward, draw it out evenly until it is fully withdrawn.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the blood is treated, as I said in the division, with the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look into the patient's throat in the sunlight, pressing their tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, draw it out completely with a small hook, or with fine forceps suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not suffice, take a feathered arrow and insert it into the patient's throat, then place a hot iron at the base of the arrow, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is continuously covered in water.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, work it into the mouth, and pour it in so that it is swallowed, and move it frequently with your hand; and as soon as the blood feels the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then smoke the patient with asafoetida using the instrument I mentioned for the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot with live coals, and cover it with a sieve pierced in the middle, and in that hole place the head of the instrument; then throw your fumigation into it, and have the patient put his head at one end, and close his mouth, so that no smoke escapes but goes directly to the blood; and the phlegm will now fall out, and if it does not fall, then continue the fumigation many times; and allow the patient thirst, and eat salted foods and alms, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for it to come forth by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats phlegm is such that when it can be seen, it resembles curved tongs for entering the throat; and it has the appearance of a bird's beak, and there are jagged edges like those of a file, so that what it grasps, it cannot let go; and here you see the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses, according to what the memory brings back later in this book from one and another, and they differ in perforation and size; and it is in two ways, one of which is in its likeness itself, and concerning those that hold moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and abscesses of soft flesh are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses that one must not pierce until the swelling is dead according to its completion; and there are some that must be pierced when they are hard, and do not die off according to their completion, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and it is left until it is ripe around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay puncturing it until it is deadened, it will harm the principal limb; when it is near the fundament, puncture it before it becomes deadened; and it is not proper to puncture an unripe abscess without complete digestion, except for one that is near the fundament, so that it does not putrefy completely, and become extended inside, and a fistula may form; and cannot heal in a long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of puncturing an abscess that is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the subsidence of fever, and the diminishment of pain and redness, and softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you perform the puncturing where the abscess depends most, and where it appears mature; and make the puncture along the body, and if the abscesses are on the hands or feet, at joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equally where there is no tenderness.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In cases of bleeding, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the palm of the hand, it is better to wait until it is confirmed to be fully digested before performing any puncture, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you puncture it before then, the venom will spread throughout the body, and it will be full of much filth; and by chance the lips and depth of it may harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And for some abscesses that need to be punctured according to the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should treat small abscesses with small punctures; and large abscesses with large punctures, and many incisions according to the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses that require cutting the center out, and scooping; when it has become as hard as leather and softened, one must act as is done with boils: and there are some that are cut into three angles, and others that are cut like the leaves of myrtle, as in abscesses on the armpits; and there are those where a round incision is made, and other cuts and similar procedures.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have an aposteme without a head, such as a superficial abscess, you must pierce it completely; and when the abscess is large, and there has been much pus collected, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at that hour, but draw out some part of it; then plug up the abscess until the next day, then draw out something again; do this little by little over many times, until all the pus is drawn out; similarly if the patient has weak constitution, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pus sometimes spurts out with great force when drawing it out, which might cause the patient to die, and you would not be at fault.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid then this chapter with great caution, and when you have punctured your abscess, wash the wound, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a full incision, bandage it with pieces of linen or old cotton; and if it is large abscesses, and there are many openings, then you must put in each one a bandage so that they come together; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and you have sewn around it, then you should fill it with old cotton or lint from linen without moisture, and tie it up until the third day; then take it out, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, then bring cold water and herbs, and moisten the cloth with it, and apply it to the bleeding area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the flow of blood continues, administer governance and care, and the powders that I have mentioned earlier in this book, and if it is winter time, and the area where the abscess is very nervous, then you must place tents and cloths moistened with wine and hot oil; and if it is summer, and the area is fleshy, then you must place cloths moistened with water and cold oil, or with wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then open the abscess and dry and treat it as necessary until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here you see the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	For small boils on the head come in various forms that are like those in cloths, such as the down of a goose, and there are many similar cases.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	Some of them are fatty and such that contain moisture like pus; and there are some that are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt about them unless the artery opposes.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work on the waist is such that you should try all the instruments called "entromissoire," of which the forms come next, and what they contain.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then cut it open from above along its length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, carefully scrape away without leaving any skin that contained that moisture, for it returns immediately if anything is left behind; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is available; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who remain from the night will run.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then restart the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that nothing remains from the night; then treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in fat tissue, cut it according to this form, longitudinally; and pour on your powders, and scrape it from all sides, and apply all your treatment to drain the contents where it lies; and if an artery opposes you, do as I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And so do for the abscess if it is stony, and in cutting and curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when you cut into the stony and moist abscess, it is easier because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there are any of these abscesses on the head where there is no moisture, and among them were the abscesses that I encountered on top of an old woman's head; and I found the abscess like a hard stone, rough and white, and it could not be broken; and if one had struck it, it would have caused as much injury as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming on the head, such as those that come at the tops of children's heads and at the roots of the ears, the incision should always be made in the lowest part to allow pus to drain out; and treat them as is appropriate.
des scrophules	scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and beneath the ears, and in angles, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and are very numerous, and grow together with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own area, as the knot and the head abscess are, as we have said; and there are many similar appearances of these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that are malignant and do not want to obey treatment.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In the one that you see has a good disposition to touch, and it resembles the color of the skin, and is soft on all sides and does not adhere to the nerves of the neck or to the artery or conduit, and is not deep; then you should cut it from above, and scrape off the skin from each part, and separate the two lips of the wound with scissors, if necessary, as we have said in head abscesses; and cut a little at a time, and be sure not to cut the nerve or vein, and do not make the incision sharp or cutting, so that your hand does not slip, and do not go too far, so you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work on it, put in the wound vitriol ground up, or some powders that coagulate blood, and hold the wound closed; and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and then begin to treat it.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is coagulated, return to your work until you complete it; then seek with your proper instrument if there remain any small scrofula, and cut them out and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, it is not necessary to cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it off with a strong double thread, and let it fall out without harm; then pack the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out all the scrofula, then you must bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them now, since there is no excess tissue due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	Then you must proceed to cut the root of it, pull out the pus, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For scrofulas that contain excess tissue, pierce where it appears necessary; and treat the puncture as previously described, allowing for drainage, then apply treatments such as ointments and similar remedies to prevent the remaining corrupted parts from further deterioration; and when the wound is thoroughly cleaned, treat with healing ointment until it is healed.
de squinance	of stretching
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote about the incision of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have stretching, it is necessary to avoid the incision of the throat called "epiglottis"; and one should not intervene in this manner, because all the veins and the phlegm of the patient are affected by a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the phlegm channel, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the danger of strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to split the epiglottis, that we make a small cut across III or IV circles, between the II circles or by the size of the incision on the surface, not in the cartilage; and those places are suitable for the section of the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from within.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, he should stretch out the skin of the neck to its full length, then cut the throat until it reaches the windpipe; and avoid the vessels that carry blood, if you see anything, and then cut the surface as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm from the windpipe which jumps forth at the place where it is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed from which one fears strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the heart, and suture all along without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be near death, and there is no other option.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he will breathe through the wound, thus being saved from death; and for this reason, the ancient doctors commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness has passed, which takes three or four days. And then they commanded to suture the wound and clean it, until it was cleaned; and I shall tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a lady took a knife and stuck it in her throat, cutting part of the flesh there; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I examined the wound and found the blood that had come out, and I realized that she had not cut any vein or vital organ in her throat, and the flesh was coming out from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and treated it until she was healed; and there came to the lady nothing but hoarseness of voice, and she returned afterwards to her disposition; for this I say that in cutting the epiglottis there need be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in the color of jet, and it often occurs in women; it has two types: natural and accidental; the natural one does not have a root cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental type has two forms, one of which is similar to fatty tissue, and the other form resembles an abscess that comes from the artery; there is fear with this, and it should not be treated by cutting except in the case where it is small, and you must examine and search throughout the interior: if you find it like fatty tissue and it cannot be connected to any vein, then cut it out as one would fat, and remove its entire covering if there is any; carefully investigate thoroughly, and treat it properly until it is completely healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	We have many ways, of which I will describe all the similarities; and now it is necessary for me to speak about all the differences that exist between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that in cases of fever and heat lasting until the boiling phase is past, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat will subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With us there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains a swelling, which is its own sac and matches the color of the skin, and begins as small as a pea, and grows large; and they are according to two types, either hard or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the treatment of the nose that you first examine and inquire about all the instruments which are called "entromissoire", according to how their form will appear in the chapter which is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of the inquiry into nasal abscesses is that you take at the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your hands little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, as it should be according to the size of the abscess; then remove the entromissoire, and be careful not to cause harm.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture flows when it cuts, whatever color it has, treat it as I have said about other abscesses; and if after the entromissoire no moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, then cut it in a cross shape, and take it with forceps, and lightly scrape each side and be careful of the coat where it lies so you can draw it out healthy with the nose; and if you cannot draw it out healthy, then take it out piece by piece so nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains there, the pus returns many times; and if a little remains, and the blood pains you, then apply the wound with some corrosive powder, and open the wound, and put on things to calm an inflamed abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the pus is great, then sew together both lips of the wound, and treat it as one who generates flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein resists or another issue arises, hasten and apply a place of broiled vitriol, and leave it for two days or three, until the wound festers, and let the blood boil; then return to scraping what remains of the pus.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of instruments used for probing, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, for encircling abscesses of fistulas; and they are also like the needles used to sew boils, and they are made of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and those that move easily are valued as being yellow, and are better for encircling curved fistulas; and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of needles are very diverse, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are needles that have two bends in three different ways; and there are needles that have three bends, and they are also in three different ways; and there are needles that have two bends, and some with only one bend, and they are in three different ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The tip of these used for cutting is sharp, and there are some that cut only from one side so as to peel the skin, so that one does not cut the vein or nerve; and among these interspersed ones are the alemeles placed in handles, so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of abscesses; and they are in three types: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only in fleshy parts such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another instrument small, resembling the shell of a fistula, according to this form, for which one stops blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed at the site suitable for cutting veins, and arteries, and sometimes follows this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the testicles of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, appearing like women's breasts; and remain deformed and swollen, and if one wishes to treat them, it must be done according to this form from this line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat and apply healing medicine to the wound, then sew together the two edges of the wound, and treat it until it is healed. If the testicle droops due to its size as often happens with women, make an incision in two flaps above it, through two similar cuts; so that one side is attached to the other at the end of each side, such that the larger part contains the smaller according to this form from line b to line g. Then scrape off the skin between the two edges and remove the fat, and apply the treatment we have described for suturing and powders, as well as what is necessary in the cure until it is healed. And if it is not yet fully healed because the patient does not want to rest or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in a corrosive ointment; leave it there until it consumes the remaining tissue and fat, then treat it until it is completely healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that occur under the buttocks are like hard scrofulous lumps containing sides, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is emptied out, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat it with ointment as appropriate until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles a scrofula, then cut it as we have said in incisions for scrofulas, and if the wound produces pus, then treat it with cauterization as we have previously described.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above it seals, abscesses often occur; similarly, it happens with a swollen vein and an abscess. And when you recognize this to be due to the artery, the abscesses are long and deep; and when you feel them with your fingers, you sense tightness; and when it is due to the vein, they appear soft and hollow; and it is foolish to cut open this abscess, especially if it is under the armpits, elbows, on the neck, and in many other places, and are very large.
