Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, it is necessary to avoid treating with iron, and one who has a rupture of the artery should also be avoided. For those suffering from swelling due to an arterial rupture, make an incision along the length; then work around the wound with scissors, carefully separating the artery from its tissues until it is fully exposed; then insert a needle underneath it, piercing through to the other side, and tie off the artery with double thread at two points as I have taught you in extracting the two arteries of the temples; then puncture between the two knots with an interposing needle so that blood flows out from there, and loosen the abscess; then apply a treatment with decoctions until the knot breaks down; if the abscess is due to a swollen vein, it is necessary to stain your hand with some of the pus around the area you hold, then insert another needle underneath where you have marked, piercing through, and place one thread across; if in doubt that the thread might not stay in place, reinsert another needle under all the abscess along the first incision’s line, tying off both threads at four points; then cut open the abscess until excess fluid comes out, then clean the wound with the heart's superfluity and leave what is tied; then apply a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil, followed by treatments of bandages and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses occur in the artery and vein, abscesses also affect the nerves when they are injured, or due to excessive labor, and similar circumstances.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this occurs more frequently in the shoulders and elbows and at all places where there are joints, and these are severe abscesses, and their color resembles the color of the skin, and they cause intense pain; and when one presses them firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not under the skin but beneath it near the heart; and it does not move in any direction, neither forward nor backward, up nor down, and those that are in joints must not be cut with a knife: for fear of causing contraction; and those that are in the head or forehead, make an incision through the scalp to the bone.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, grasp it with forceps and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it on an incision, then peel it, remove it, and close the wound by stitching, until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	large hanging pouches
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the abdomen and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" by its resemblance to them; the root is subtle, and the lump is large; there are both small and very large ones. I saw a person who had two of these in their abdomen that looked more like fungi than anything else, with no difference, they were white, had fine roots, and were somewhat split, and moisture corroded them quickly.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I weighed them and found eighteen ounces in one, and six in the other, and when performing the incision, you should observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist with a fine texture; then cut it with a broad spatula, and have the cautery by fire ready at hand.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when cutting, there are often excessive flows of blood, and if the blood continues to flow, quickly proceed with cauterization; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the iron incision, take a well-made linen thread, tie it around the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; then remove it, but do not stop tying the linen thread until you cut the artery, and carefully separate it by working with it; and if the roots are thick, be careful when cutting them to avoid harming the abdomen, but you can safely cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not regrow; finally heal the wound, and ensure that you do not cut the tendon which is red in color and difficult to work with and has a milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an embedded abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers shortly thereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the swelling is strong
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the swelling comes from a cautery on a wound or cut on the surface, and it is on the belly and some boils appear, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness; and if it is from the rupture of the surface and from the outlet of the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the skin, and it is a light thing without pain, and clearly has diverse outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the outlet of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses on both sides it swells up, and then returns, and perhaps it is hard, and greatly enlarges at the entrance to the bath and for heavy labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and you can easily tell when you press it with your hand, as there is no resistance; and if it is due to blood, you can see by these signs the large and hard abscesses that are fixed according to quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft upon touching, and in this work, you must look to see whether the appearance is from artery blood, or vein blood, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear about it, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, concerning the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is from the intestine or the bladder, you must instruct the patient to hold their breath, lie flat, and then puncture all around the swelling; then have them lie still between your hands, then work around the area where you marked for the entire span of the swelling; then extend half of the abscess above halfway with a large hook; then bind it tightly with strong thread or silk cord firmly, so that the skin is compressed by the bandage; then work on the extended part of the abscess lying on the bandage, and place your index finger to feel for the intestine; if you find it caught in the binding, release it and pull the intestine out of the abdominal cavity; and if you find the bladder, grasp it with forceps and cut off the excess; and if an artery or vein opposes this, proceed gently around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two pieces of thread across what you need to pierce in a cross shape; then squeeze the abscess into four parts on the needles, and if necessary, remove the needles when it has softened and begun to decay, then treat the area as needed, cut away the pus as we have said; and extract any blood or moisture that you find, then treat the wound as required, and close the wound.
dou chancre	of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division about the similarities of ulcers and how one should treat them with medicines, and how one should avoid treatment with iron; we say that ulcers often originate in moist areas, and great caution is necessary in their treatment. The ancients stated that when ulcers are in places where they can be scraped out, such as those on the breasts, thighs, and similar locations, you should remove them entirely when they are in the beginning stage; but when they are large and old, it is not advisable to approach them, for I have never seen any healing from them, nor has anyone before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the procedure, when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile if necessary; then make the patient fast if there is obvious repletion; then position the patient properly for the procedure; then apply your forceps or hooks to the ulcer and remove hair from all sides thoroughly without leaving anything behind; let the blood flow freely and press firmly with your hand or some object; and if the outflow of blood causes difficulty in cutting an artery or vein, cauterize until the bleeding stops; then treat further as needed until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of hydropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already described in the division the similarities of hydropsy, and how the gathering of fluid is formed, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: it is called "eclites" alone; and one should not touch with iron in these two similarities: namely, tympanites and yposarche, because this is a deadly thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of hydropsy which is called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not succeed, then look if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides hydropsy, such as coughing and releasing gas and similar things; do not touch with iron in these cases, because there is doubt involved; and if you see that the patient is of strong constitution, and he does not have any other illness but hydropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then proceed thus: lift the patient up straight in your hands, and let the assistants press the belly by pushing out the fluid to the lowest part of the abdomen, then take the spatumile iron according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be cuts from both sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	With a point, and let it not be so deep that it can reach the intestines when inserted, nor should it bleed; then observe if the dropsy is towards the intestines: if so, you must cut above the navel three fingers wide below the ribcage; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, make your incision on the left side of the navel three fingers; and if it is due to menstruation, do it on the right side, but the patient should not lie on the incision so that excess fluids do not flow into a weak area; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and pull out your hand throughout the spatumile between the skin and the subcutaneous tissue as if in flaying to the size of a thumbnail or around; then pierce the subcutaneous tissue until the spatumile comes to an open place, which is where the water lies, then draw it forth, and insert this instrument of which here is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a fine silver chain, and it is made of iron or brass, and has in the middle part one small hole; and on the side, three holes; and two on another side, and one on another; and the head is cut like a quill feather, and this is the form of the incision that the writer makes when cutting the quill.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the alembic, so that when the instrument comes to the liquid, it now descends upon the instrument; empty then half or a third of it, for if you empty more than necessary at this hour, by chance the patient may die due to the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls unconscious, or approaches death; but empty according to its quantity and according to what the conditions of the patient's strength indicate, and his pulses; then pull out the instrument and retain the liquid, and it is now retained by the heart which stops up the hole that is above the surface, about which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then restart the instrument another day if you see the patient suffering from it, and draw off a small amount of fluid; do this for some days, and guard against overdoing it so that no more than a little liquid remains.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you are unsure about the patient, and leave much water in them, treat with burial or hot sand, and by much sweating or bath and in the sun, and advise to drink less; and treat with drying medicines until he is well, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	about the swelling of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who have no opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary to pierce it immediately with a very fine spatula according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place a fine cloth in the opening and tie it there for three or four days, and when he wishes to urinate, remove the cloth, allow him to urinate, and then replace the cloth; and perhaps no cloth is necessary, because the urine that comes out will not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose opening is small should be treated with a cloth of flax as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the opening in its place are deformed, for some are born with the opening at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis up; and they cannot copulate because the matter cannot reach the testicles, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of work is that the patient lies supine on his back, then place the tip of the rod against the head and apply it as evenly as the width of a feather shaft, so that the aperture fits precisely; and be wary of blood loss which occurs often, and if it happens, stop the bleeding with what stops blood, and treat the wound until he is healthy.
des pustules de la verge	pustules of the shaft
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these albathe appear in the shaft, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh; there are both malignant and non-malignant ones; you must take them out with a fine lancet, clean and treat them all, then apply cotton moistened with Egyptian ointment; then cure with diafinicon ointment until he is healthy.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of foul color and spreading, then you must apply cauterization to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the ulcer is in a place where part of it is inside the flesh and part outside, then you must remove the part that is inside first; and when it is adhered, treat the part that is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it all at once, the edges of the ulcer are not secure and may perforate, leading to blackening and corruption in the area; thus, you must excise everything that is blackened and corrupted, then apply a plaster made from pomegranate rind and vinegar, and continue treating it until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, then treat with a lunar cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauterization helps with two conditions simultaneously: namely, bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupt and retracted, it is necessary to insert a lead tube into the urethra so that the patient can urinate through it; and when hair grows at the head of the penis, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, whether due to wound or abscess, then it is necessary to excise it with a sharp instrument until the ligaments are loosened, and release the head of the penis from all sides; and if it is difficult to describe this procedure, then excise a little bit at the head of the penis and skin with a spatula, then carefully separate them, and place a fine linen strip soaked in cold water between them so that no further growth occurs.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like the separation of continuity as other wounds are; nevertheless, when we perform this work by our will, and properly on children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the least harmful for their well-being.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the majority of masters and surgeons who performed circumcision around the glans, and forcefully, and entirely with a new blade; it was dangerous because there are two layers, and perhaps they cut the one above while leaving the one below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now it must be cut again, and the pain is doubled, and in the treatment of the nail there is no certainty about the tip of the member; and in treating the nail the iron may slip by chance, and the work will run amok, and many times they are born such that they do not need treatment, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the treatment that is done with force to the entire limb of thread I have found the goodness through experience, for the force cuts precisely both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, cut evenly in one single motion; but let the thread be tightly wrapped around the skin. And the manner of the first treatment is such that if the child understands, make him think that you are only tying the thread around his penis just for a moment, then cheer him up in all ways possible; then hold him straight between your hands, and place your fingers or tools underneath so he cannot see them; then touch your hand to the penis and blow on it, then pull upwards until the head of the penis is fully out; then clean well from the accumulated dirt, then tie securely with a double thread below the scrotum, and bind both sides; hold firmly by the second binding at the pouch and index finger, cut between the two bindings, raise the part quickly and draw the head of the penis; let the blood flow slowly drop by drop, for it is the safest way; then apply powder upon powder mixed with a yolk of an egg beaten with rose water, prepared well with fresh rose oil, leave it on until the next day, and treat it further as needed until he is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the force for cleansing is thus: the two edges should be blunt and should be as thick as a finger equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in cleansing occurs when the pus inside flows to the incision; then it is necessary that you extend it to your nail, just as one would with an abscessed boil; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it to your nail, hold it with forceps, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three days, and the area below the groin is swollen, let it be until the abscesses are sufficiently abated, and lightly scrape it; cut it as much as you can without harming the part of the groin, for it will do no harm to it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, treat the place of a hot wound with powder, which we have mentioned in the chapter on powders, and if one cuts into the heart too much, and it goes beyond measure, it will not harm; treat it as we have said until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	from the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the obstruction by a stone, or congealed blood, or bladder, or dead flesh, or similar things, which we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone that is jammed at the neck of the bladder, then it must be that the patient sit on his knees; and place their feet on their back, and stretch out their belly from above the back, and have the patient pull in their abdomen as much as they can; and then this constrains the neck of the bladder to expel the stone upwards, thus releasing the urine; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument that is called "syringe", here is its form: it should be made of fine light silver, like a feather of an arrow; and it should be a length of half a palm at the head, and it should be fine.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of urination is that you take a double thread, and tie at the top a pouch of wool or cotton, and put the end of the thread inside the syringe; then cut off the excess wool and push it all the way to the top of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and have the patient sit on a chair, and lubricate the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and vinegar water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the base of the penis, then wrap the penis upwards towards the body; then push the syringe forward to the bladder, and the patient will feel it coming up to the empty area, and this is not done according to this order unless what guides it as it goes is crooked; then pull out the thread little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out again, and let the urine flow; and repeat with the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient feels relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When pus or blood comes to the bladder, and there is an accumulation of putrefaction, and you wish to administer liquids and medications, use all the instrument called "clepsydre," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed and has III openings: II on one side, and I on the other, as you see; and the place where the medicine enters should be such that it stops up the tube tightly so that water can be drawn out and poured in when necessary; and when you wish to introduce your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the syringe in the liquid, and draw with the drawer inside; thus, you will draw the liquid into the syringe, then push it forcefully back in; thus, the liquid will enter, reaching the bladder so that the patient feels it; this is the form of a subtle enema used to cleanse the bladder: it is as follows:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or brass, and the head is higher; and behind the chest where the ligament falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the liquid you wish to use for enema, then tie between the two breasts with a strong double thread, and heat the pot of that liquid over the fire; then insert the tip of the enema into the rectum, then press your hand on the bladder gradually until the patient feels that all the liquid has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle out of it, and pierce it roundly around; then insert the string firmly through these holes, then join the circle as one joins a sieve, and put inside what you wish of oil and liquid and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand gradually until all the liquid comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already stated in the division the methods of stones and their extraction along with medicines; and I have described the difference between a stone formed in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in which stone one should operate for cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is formed in the bladder happens more often to children, and this is a sign that the urine leaps from the bladder similar to acute urine in its subtlety; and one can see hairiness, and the patient's penis itches, and he scratches many times, and then becomes swollen; and much of these leaps are the foundation; and healing for children until they are four years old is easier, and very difficult for the elderly, and moderate for those who are between youth and old age; and the treatment is lighter for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient with an enema, to draw out all the feces that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes hinders in seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and lift him up and move towards his backside so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes from a high place; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands should be behind his thighs, so that the bladder is completely tilted downward; then seek it and feel inside; if you sense the stone in the space, now hurry to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall upon touching all around, moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is male, or your middle finger, if the patient is a fully grown female; and insert it into his/her fundament, and seek the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, push it towards the neck of the bladder; then press upon your finger, and guide it out where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to spread apart his thighs with his right hand, and with his left hand remove the skin that is underneath the scrotum in the area where the incision will be made; then apply the cautery cutting instrument, which this is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make an incision between the scrotum and the anus, not in the middle but on the side of the left thigh; let it be straight over the stone, with both ends reaching towards the anus, and make the opening wide enough to pass through easily, while narrow inside according to the size of the stone, so that pressing does not cause discomfort to the area around the anus; and know there are some stones with corners and edges: these are difficult to remove; and there are others that lie beneath, resembling a thorn or a round object, whose removal is easier.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For him then who has angles and margins, make the size larger; and if it does not jump, you must clamp with pliers that are like a file at the head, to force out the stone so that it does not escape; or you place under the instrument curved at the head; and if you cannot manage it thus, then enlarge the hole, and if the blood peels off, clamp it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, first push the larger one towards the bladder neck, then proceed upwards, then pull out forcefully, and the smaller ones after if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, you must wait and make a larger incision.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes immediately so that the place cannot close; but nevertheless strive to pull it out, or with pliers in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloes and dragon's blood, and bind it tight, and put a damp cloth over it in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then lift the patient onto his shoulder, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, wash the area thoroughly with oil and water, then treat it with diafinicon ointment and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses and corrosions come in the wound, and clots of blood in the bladder, which cause retention of urine, occurring mixed with it: apply your hand to the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains there, it will rot the bladder; then wash the wound with water and herbs and wool, and help in all ways you know until it is healed; and it must be that every time you treat it, you tie the two thighs together, and apply medicines to the site.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra channel, and stuck there, so that the urine cannot pass; then treat it as I say thus, that you cut it multiple times, but be cautious with this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tested this in this way.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron fork according to this form and have three prongs fixed in one handle:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take some thread and tie it around the penis below the stone so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then gently insert the fork into the penis until it reaches the stone; and rotate the fork with your hand on the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; then urine will come soon, and press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is immediately fractured, and urine passes with it, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this for some reason that prevents it, tie a thread below the stone and another above, then cut the penis directly on top of the stone between the two threads, then extract the stone, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood which is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the women's stone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone occurs in women, and if it does occur once, the treatment is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows well enough to expose herself to doctors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more firm than the stone of the man, why it must be made a deeper cut, and great fear there is. And if necessities mount to thee, it behooves that thou takest a midwife well knowing, and at pains thou findest one, and if thou findest not, seek a subtle surgeon; and presenteth unto her a bailiff well wise in the life of women, or a woman who knoweth part of the art, and commandeth her that she doth what thou commandeth from the inquiry of the stone; and regard much well whether the woman is a virgin: then it behooves to put her right hand into the fundament and seek the stone; and if she findeth it, constrain it beneath her right hand, and commend unto her that she put her right hand in where the patient is and seek and press her left hand upon the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut above the stone at the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the anus, where the passage is prepared, and feel for the stone in that part; and do not move her foot above or below the stone, and let the incision be small initially; then insert a probe into the incision, if you feel the stone enlarge the wound until the stone can come out freely, and know that there are many types of stones: namely small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and with edges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	know the signs to understand the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the flesh weakens, then place powdered vitriol at the site and hold it for an hour until the flesh hardens; then return to your work until the stone is out, and have the instruments I told you about for extracting stones from men to assist in your work; and if the flesh weakens, and this is from the artery that has been cut, then apply powder to the site and bind with cloths and bandages, and do not repeat that procedure, and leave the stone and do not extract it, as the patient might die by chance; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the swelling subsides, then return to your work, until the stone has been expelled.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aqueous retention is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white matter that dislodges from the heart of the testicles, which contains the egg; and it is called "white matter," and sometimes it is properly within the membrane of the egg, so one thinks it might be another egg; and this occurs in the skin of the testicle between the white matter we have mentioned; and such a thing happens without pain.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this retention is due to weakness that affects the testicles, and this matter spreads.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: where it declines to yellow, or is without redness, or black, or aqueous white, and this happens more; and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is in the white pus we have mentioned, then the abscesses are abundant, I measure long as the shape of an egg, and do not reveal the testicles, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper tissue, then the abscesses are abundant with part of an egg, and because of this, people think it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white pus, one can feel it well; therefore when you wish to know the color of the moisture, you should examine thoroughly all around, as described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introduction, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with an iron instrument, the patient must be bled according to our power and the fullness of his body; then lay him on his back upon something slightly raised, and place many cloths under him; then sit on his left side, and order the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod along one of the two ribs below the navel; then take the scalpel lightly, and cut the skin between the long part down to near the base, and let your incision be entirely straight until you reach the white area, and peel off the skin delicately as much as possible; then pierce the white area fully with water through one wide opening, and drain all the fluid, and then apply bandages, pulling the white area upwards; do not touch the bladder but only the white part; cut everything around it carefully so that if you do not cut properly, the fluid will return; and if the urethra jumps during your work, then reposition it in its place after completing the treatment of the white area; then join the two sides of the bladder at a seam, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to tie off the vessels that are suspensory, fearing the loss of blood; then cut the cord entirely suspensory, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the fluid is gathered in two parts together, know that these are two roots; cut the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and place in the wound wool soaked in rose oil; and place another layer of wool soaked in wine and oil on top, and cover with doubled cloths, and tie it all up according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and wrap them with wool according to this appearance and sew them together at the waistband of the trousers, one extending from the buttocks up to the back, and the other covering the groin area; and both ends should be gathered into a knot in the trouser loop; and sometimes this root is treated with cautery instead of iron cutting, so take a small knife-shaped cautery, cut through the skin of the cord, and heat it as we have said, until the white fluid that contains the fluid becomes visible; then take the cautery according to this form, pierce the white surface with hooks, and scrape it with this hot fine cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And cut in all ways that you can, until everything is clean; and make sure the fire does not touch the eye; and know that this work is safer; and move with caution to prevent blood loss, and handle the operations delicately; and if anything goes against you, whether an abscess or blood loss or something else, then treat what opposes you according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not wish to endure this procedure due to its horror, then proceed with perforation as I told you; and when you are certain by the signs we have mentioned that there is watery pus present, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess from below across the entire breadth of the spatumile, making the puncture in line with the body's length; ensure the perforation is wide so all the fluid can flow out freely; place cotton over the site and secure it, allowing any remaining fluid to drain; treat the wound until it heals; if white cloth does not allow the fluid to escape from the wound opening, then insert a feather or instrument used for treating hydropic fluids as described earlier; expand the cavity of the wound, knowing that the fluid will return after about six months or so, and when it reassembles as before, the patient will pass their days in this manner.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch there are many fears and positions, for which it seems better to leave it as is; and I will tell you about the work and similar cases of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses occur in the body, and especially in the testicles; and this is due to various causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is due to excessive acidity and humidity spread in the testicles, or from impact; and the color of the abscess corresponds to the color of the skin; and there is no pain, and it is a severe abscess; and sometimes an abscess may be purulent, fearful, and stony, with a reddish color, and at times it comes from damage to an artery or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to an artery, it is known by the hot disposition of the abscess when you press it with your fingers; and it must not be touched.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	One who is affected by a swollen vein is known by its disposition and the expression when touched with the fingers, and one can properly treat this condition as well as others; cut the groin area, then place the egg upward, drain the pus from the white surface, and free the suspensory band around the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already swollen with these newly grown tissues, then you must drain the egg and cut it; and if it is inflamed on the surface or inside the vessels, then you must free all of that area and cut it completely round.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is at the rear, then you must cut it all away, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is complete, apply the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a covering similar to the scrotum, with softening of the testicles, and the patient suffers greatly when he moves; and the treatment for this disease is as difficult as the previous one, yet we will tell you about it according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you seat the patient on a raised chair, then place the suspensory of the testicles down to your hands, covering all the vessels which are near the penis, and hold them tightly and stretch them firmly; then cut with a broad and sharp spatula across the vessels until they are exposed, and then scrape from each side as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples; then place an needle where there is double thread, and tie it at the first spot where the vein comes out, and tie it again at the other end; then cut them directly in the middle according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moisture; then treat the wound as with others when bandaging, so that some vessels may fall which nourish one of the testicles; for by this there is no harm, and if all the vessels come to a vein, it is necessary to draw out the testicles from all the vessels; so that the testicle does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot be aided.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the fracture of the cheekbone
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrence of this rupture is through the section that comes from the cheekbone, or by stretching on the abdomen in the area where the angles are, causing the intestines to descend from this fracture to one of the groins; and this rupture is either from the cheekbone itself, or from its extension, and these two manners come from many causes: such as percussion, jumping, lifting, carrying heavy loads, and similar things; and when it is due to an extension of the cheekbone, it happens little by little over a long period of time, not suddenly; and the abscesses are equal up to the bottom because the cheekbone presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the section of the cheekbone, that it causes sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear differently, near the skin, because of the exit of the intestines and the body withdrawing from the cheekbone.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines descend with the bowel, and are retained within, causing great pain for the patient, especially when they are compressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments there is fear, for which one should avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method of work is that you instruct the patient to push his intestines back into the wound with his hand if it can enter; then secure your hands around his neck, and lift his thighs; then place your hand above his abdomen, and carefully cut all the skin from the groin area according to what is needed to open the wound, ensuring that the bladder can protrude; then peel off the fatty layer underneath the skin of the groin until the hard white fat tissue is exposed on all sides; then insert your index finger into the space behind the testicle, between the hard white fat tissue beneath the scrotal skin and the second layer of tissue, and separate what lies behind the testicle from the second layer of tissue; then move the hard white fat tissue to the top with your right hand, and lift the testicle onto the fatty tissue towards the waist; instruct the assistant to raise the testicle upwards and release the bandage at the back;
