inquire whether there is any intestine wrapped around the hard white fat tissue, and if you find anything, return it below the belly; then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten strands, and insert it into the rear part of the fatty tissue behind the scrotal skin; after the waist, cut the hair that appears from the threads until there are four strands remaining; then arrange them one on top of another in the form of a cross, and tie down the fatty tissue we mentioned beneath the scrotal skin with a strong thread from two sides; then wrap up the strands of hair and tie them firmly from both sides so that no small vessels can enter and cause an abscess to occur; then apply a bandage according to the first long bandage in double thickness, and after these two bandages leave exposed at the bottom part below the scrotal skin about twice its width; then apply the rest following the roundness of the testicle; then cut around the area beneath the scrotal skin as we have mentioned previously regarding the skin and the wound; then place wet wool soaked in oil on the wounds, and apply the bandages we have described.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white vein we have mentioned is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and leave the ligature until it falls off by itself; and if it delays in falling, soak it in warm water, and place what we have said on it until it falls off; then treat the wound with other methods, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I have never seen anyone dare to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done like the condition where the intestines are involved, in such a way that you tie off the vessels, above the navel lightly towards the back; then cut into it, and treat the abscess with what we have described, until the vessels fall off; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and it is apparent; and no part of the intestines descends to the genitals, but if they do descend, it is dangerous and requires constant care; yet if it remains too long at this point, the wound or the suture heals improperly, causing the intestines to descend; this happens because of the extension of the suture that is in the groin, as we have said, for it becomes stretched, then softened and swollen and apparent; and the treatment is by cautery, as we have previously mentioned; but sometimes it is treated with an iron in this way: the patient lies on their back between your hands, then incise the swollen area according to a length of three digits; then remove the suture that is under the skin as follows, then take the needle and place it over the apparent part of the suture; press it firmly against the belly, then sew up both sides of the suture on top of the needle head; then pull out the needle head without cutting into the suture or extending the wound, as I have told you in the treatment of hernia; finally treat it according to the method for treating wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, bind the wound and treat the injury until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The tissue is tight, and there is no appearance of tearing, and the cauterizations are soft in this place, and closer to being beneficial.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	from the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	The skin of the testicles is often softened in some men because the tissues inside are softened, and it appears milky; and when one wishes to treat this condition, have the patient lie on his back, and cut the soft skin over the natural skin; then stitch together the two lips at a seam, and if you wish, sew the excess soft skin along three or four seams firmly; then cut between the seams, and treat it as other wounds until it is healed, and remove the stitches.
dou chastrement	of the punishment/training/treatment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You know that punishment is condemned in our law, and for that reason it would please me not to speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary except for two reasons: one being that the doctor knows how to respond when asked, and knows the treatment; and the other, because we often need to castrate some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that castration is performed in two ways: either by traction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method we perform by traction, we make the animal sit in hot water until the testicles become softened and hang down; then hold them with your hand until they are retracted and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the castration of animals: you should anesthetize the beast, and press the skin over its testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory bandage, and cut each one in one stroke after thoroughly flaying them; leave some soft fat and the fine fat that lies on the vessels; this method of castration is gentler than that done by traction, because with traction there may remain some part of the testicles by chance, causing the animal to desire lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Regarding hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermafroditism is of two kinds in men: one is that between the two testicles it has the appearance as defined by nature for a woman, including hair, and sometimes the urine is enclosed there.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is for women, and place upon the thigh as thick as a rod and two fingers.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for men and women is that you cut away all adjacent tissues, and treat them as other wounds; in the second method, for men whose urine sprays over the skin of the genitals, there is no specific treatment.
de la tentigene	of the tendinitis
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a tissue attached to the natural part, so much so that it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should dye the excess of the tentigene with your hand or fingernails and cut it lightly; do not go too deep so that no blood flows, then treat it as you would another wound until it heals; and for another tissue that arises at the mouth of the womb, remove it, and perhaps it will heal, and it resembles a horn, and for this reason the ancients called it "horn disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you treat it as we have said regarding tendon treatment, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is erratic when the nature of a woman's body is not understood, or when the passage is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental due to illness that affects it; or due to thick or thin secretions adhering to it, and these can form firmly in the belly, or in the sides, or elsewhere; and prevent conception, childbirth, and perhaps menstruation; and knowledge of this comes from examining the body.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If constipation is imminent, I want you to use either two fingers or the right (finger).
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a soft suppurating abscess and it is near the two books, hurry and do this: place your two thumbs together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then pull apart the two books firmly until the soft abscess is exposed, and above the swelling; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on the area, and have the woman lie with a man each day so that she cannot stand.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the abscess is hard and thick, then you should cut it with a scalpel as thin as a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of flesh growth, suspend it by a thread and cut it; and have medicines to stop bleeding, such as honey, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with an abundance of egg white; then dress the wound with a strip of cloth wide enough that the wound cannot close; and treat it in this manner for a long time, and dress it with a linen bandage; then continue treatment until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when flesh becomes inflamed in a wound, it should be cut according to this manner, except for embedded abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For in the case of an embedded abscess in the wound, one should not touch it to cut.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are protrusions of veins that usually occur without cause, and when hemorrhoids become old they turn hard; and we have already mentioned in the division their appearances, and the signs, and I will say here those that can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and hard lumps, when they are fully formed in the wound, do not hurt to touch, so it is not necessary to treat them with a cautery.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who have a sore on the mouth, which can be felt, are those who can be treated by scraping.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then stretch the altar with pliers, and cut it at its roots; then apply powder made of medicines that restrain blood, such as oak bark and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate rind, gall, and similar ingredients, and then take oatmeal, mix it with honey and grease, and apply this as a poultice to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him inhale cupping glasses on the back and breasts without injuring them; then take flax, and soak it in juice of plantain or in juice of elder with old wine, and apply to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and what is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, so it must be cut as I said about the thelul; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	for abscesses of the flesh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the flesh, such as canker and stone abscess and herpes and ulcers and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary then that I speak in this treatise about the hot abscess which comes to the leg, which is not of the abscesses that are collected by bowe; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look to see if the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Do not hurry to pierce it, but let it die down until the pain is eased; and then make the patient sit on a chair, and have two small chairs where he can recline, and support his back and bring his legs together behind the thigh; and let his thighs be spread out, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good cloth; then give him the tool to work on the mouth of the leg, which follows the form below; and it is necessary that when you want to apply this instrument, you insert the tip first to know the depth of the leg so that what enters inside the instrument does not go deeper than it should and does not hurt the patient; and if the tool is larger, cover the depth of the leg with cloths so that the tool does not harm him; and he must place the cone of the instrument on top, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is open, and it is cut gently by hand, then it must be excised at the top, to the sphenoid bone; and when the pus is evacuated, then you should put into the wound cloths soaked in rose oil or in green oil of vinegar; place the cloth over the wound on a clean linen bandage soaked in water or chamomile boiled; then treat after two days of ointment application as needed, until it heals; and sometimes lift the bandage and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then water with roots of lily and wormwood long cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is placed on the bandage, then you must avoid heating it with iron, but treat it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman press down, and desire to smell the air: then the child hastens to come forth; at that moment you know that this childbirth follows a natural course, and its passage is under his head, and the secondine with him; and when you see these signs, it is fitting to gently press her belly so that the child comes out quickly; for when he descends under his head, then the secondine comes with him, and the child is cleansed of its superfluities by proper cleansing; and one who comes forth otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes comes upon its feet, and forth the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes upon its belly, or side, and is turned about by chance onto its neck, and in other evil figures; therefore it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these matters, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out naturally onto its head, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and if her strength is weak, then have her sit on a stool, which women hold; and give her a drink of oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then place between her two nostrils the small spoon depicted here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the membrane, and slice it to where the moisture inside comes out; and press the woman's abdomen so that the child descends, and if it does not descend, then enema her with fenugreek muscillago mixed with sesame oil; then have her take condisi and sneeze, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both arms come out first, then you must gently reset them little by little; and if they cannot go back in, place the woman on a stool, and lift her feet up high; then raise the stool off the ground, but ensure the woman does not fall when it is raised; and if the arms do not enter and the child dies, cut the arms with the knife provided here, extract the child, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the birth of the child upon its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes up on its feet, it is necessary to lift them high; then turn them little by little until they are straight; then take one foot and stretch it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps up to the thighs, command it to grasp them, and make it sneeze from condition; if it jumps further, as God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not go further as we have said, turn it little by little until it is according to its natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will move easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if the heat does not come as we have described, take muscillaige of aloes, and oil of cumin seeds, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; then place within it the nature of the woman, and apply this ointment, then make her sit in warm water up to below her ribs; and when she is moistened below, give her an enema of myrrh, and put it inside, and let her have one hour; then make her sit on the commode, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and gently massage her belly, for the child now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the delivery of the child upon her knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this manner, place your hands upon its back little by little; then let her lie down on her side, and hang her feet downwards, and lie her flat on the bed; then bend her arms little by little, and then massage her hands over her belly, and remove the cushions below so that she is prepared to go downward; and if the child does not move, take its feet and move them forward, then move its belly upwards, then place your hands inside; and bring out the child little by little; and instruct the woman to pull as soon as the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes from the wide a hand hanging
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary for the surgeon to return the hand: if it cannot be returned, make the woman stand and walk; if she cannot walk, have her lie on the bed, and raise her legs straight; then administer the medicine that I have described; and if she does not give birth, have her sit on a chair, then study how to return the hand; and observe the child according to its natural form, and make her sneeze, and command her to hold onto it until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child upon its neck, and with its hands spread out, and its face turned towards its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the bailiff hold her hand, then turn it bit by bit, and move the water gently; and when it is even, apply the natural mixture of earth and oil as we have said, then instruct her to move it bit by bit; and once you have done this, make her sit on a chair and tell her to grasp something; and then make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner for the entire second part
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to applying force in this manner to the entire second part, cut the membrane at your nail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child can pass over its face and neck, cut from the mouth so that it is not obstructed, and turn the child; then place the child inside as it should be, and instruct the woman to grasp something: then gently extract.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of the issue of the hamstrings
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that hamstrings often grow multiple times, and sometimes three or four grow; and this is not a strange thing, it happens occasionally.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	This is a strange thing, and they do not live, except rarely; I know that they are multiplied, and are separated by the muscle that divides them, which is attached to the buttocks; and sometimes they emerge as naturally as one whole, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they emerge severely, then treat them as we have said, and let the hand be subtle, and do quickly and gently what it does; and do so as it is worth to heal for salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed at the first month I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or sometimes up to XV, and they are entirely shaped in the form of a child according to the measurement of the wise physician, and it is necessary that he carefully examines all of them, for perhaps similar things may happen; therefore act accordingly as is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman of a dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and there is no expulsion, and you are constrained to work with your hands; it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound health, and has not had any accidents where she fears death; it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back, and her thighs inclined downward, and her legs raised; then the assistant holds her from two sides, or wherever she lies so that she does not slide down during the descent of the child; then rub her mouth with a month's worth of oil mixed with muscilleges of hellebore and fenugreek and flax seeds, then smear the physician’s hands with these oils and muscilleges; then gently insert your fingers into the womb lightly, then look for one place where you can put the hooks that are suitable for this situation, and be wary if the child is prepared to come down headfirst; then fix the hooks in its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the chin or in the forceps or near the ribs, and if the descent is from feet first, place them at the heels and on the middle ribs; it is necessary that he holds the hook with his right hand, and places the handle between both sides of his left hand, and gently inserts all his fingers, placing the hooks in any of these places we mentioned until something comes out empty; this is the form of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert against the other hook, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is even; and then extend evenly by moving from one side to the other, to help them come out, and let the hooks be toothed to hold the muscles, as shown in this form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if any part remains, smear the sides with some of your oil, and put it in that part, and pull out the other part; and if anything remains, place this hook higher up, and do so until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and he cannot bring it back for grasping, then you must wrap around the finger until it all comes out; then tie it at the joint of the palm or with a knot, and do the same for the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the infant is large and it is narrow at the opening, where there is a severe headache gathered, then you must insert the spatumile spineous between your two fingers, cut open the head and extract the fluid; or you can shave it with the instrument called “almidach”, from which the shape comes with the instruments in the chapter that follows this one; and so similarly proceed if the infant has a large head naturally; and then pull out the bones with forceps, and if the head jumps out and is held by the force, let them be split until the moisture that is inside the rear opening can come out; and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it so that the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the adjustment to the mouth of the socket is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is tight in the abdomen or breast, then you must stretch it with a sling wrapped around the hand; and cut open the abdomen or breast until the moisture inside flows out; and if another member has been removed and the head remains, then put your fingers deep into the socket, and pull them to the mouth of the socket; then insert one finger or two, and pull forcefully; and if the mouth of the socket is constricted due to a hot abscess that has come there, then do not work on it, but instead apply moist and oily remedies; and the remedy as plasters, and use aqueous solutions that soften and moisturize.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can make it even, then treat it as we have said for the living child; and if one has no power over it, then cut it up piece by piece, and leave nothing of the membrane behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, treat it as we have said for hot abscesses that come with fever; and if blood discharge occurs, then place it in constricting water, and treat it with other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom the fetus in her womb had been dead, and then another was conceived, but that one too was stillborn.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, abscesses came to her mouth, and it swelled so much that it burst, and began to pus profusely.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I pondered for a long time, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied an adhesive plaster, and out came a bone, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly, for there are no bones in the abdomen.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it must be the bone of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I explored the wound and extracted many bones until the woman was in a much better state; and for some time thereafter, she occasionally discharged pus from the site; and I recall this chapter only because when masters encounter an unusual thing, they should seek to understand it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the joint to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here follows the form of the binder, which the books have; and for two turns at the two shoulders of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be finer than the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the shaft should be two fingers wide, and the margin of the wood one finger thick, and a length of one palm and a half; and between the two limbs there should be two projections of this same wood, which are firmly fixed in each, about half a palm long or a bit more; and these two projections are placed in the mouth of the joint to open when the two horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony wood or boxwood, resembling pincers; and it should have two heads with two attachments, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the vagina with the entire instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, her feet hanging down and legs spread apart, then place the two attachments together in the vagina, holding the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then work your hand along the entire instrument as you did with the pincers equally, according to the size you wish to open the mouth of the vagina, until it gives way as much as she desires.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all equipped at the top, and their appearances vary; and when the doctors have them prepared, they become more efficient in their work, and higher quality for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument because you have not prepared it, for their need is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze with something dry, and hold your hands over her mouth and nose; if she jumps because of this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make holes in its cover, and place herbs that can open the mouth of the fetus inside, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, costmary, and centaury; all these herbs or some of them should be cooked in water over the fire; then put one end of a tube into the pot's hole, and the other end in the mouth of the fetus, and hold it tightly so that the vapors enter the fetus; then make her sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	The second joint moves quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and does not move as desired, command the patient to moisten her left hand in linseed oil or muscilaginous of althea, and then place it on the area naturally, and seek the second joint; and when she has found it, take hold of it and extend it little by little straight, so that the tendons do not slip during extraction; but it must be moved gently to the right and left, and then pulled; it will come out and release.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the tendon's opening is tight, we have mentioned the cure of sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not move from all that we have said, be careful not to forcefully pull; but it must be that what is at the tendon’s opening, you tie it to the woman's thigh, then administer an ointment enema tetrafarmacson; this will soften and reset it, and it will come out freely; but nonetheless, when it softens if there comes a bad odor to the stomach and head, and bleeds the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, appropriate fumigations are necessary for these conditions: some of the ancients have found fumigation with parsley and dried figs to be effective.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates a woman to retain her flowers and secondines is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is made of glass resembling a tube, with the head fine in the structure and the ends wide over the fire; and place the fumigation above the coals, and let the smoke be until it is spent, then start another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, instead it is sealed with a fine substance: therefore, the midwife must pierce that substance at its proper place, and should not do so with a sharp spatula, but rather handle it carefully so as not to touch it; then apply wool moistened in wine and oil, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that he will stay in place, put a chain through the hole, and leave his hands free for days, and remove it when the child wishes to go to chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this obstruction comes from the sudden closure of a wound or abscess; then it is necessary to cut through that closure: it should be treated as we have said about the chain of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from inside the anus are nodations, and those that come near the anus to escape, or in the space between the two parts, may have one fistula or more; and when these nodations are old, they work, and sometimes moisture awakens blanching or subtle boils, and at times these fistulas are persistent; and they are recognized by what comes out with excretion or flatulence when the patient has a bowel movement, and occasionally a worm may come out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate to the bladder, and to half of the penis; and reach to the knee joint, and to the root of the thigh.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows whether the fistula extends to the anus or not: and it is that you insert your index finger into the anus, and insert a fine needle of linen or iron into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is curvature, insert a slender tent of flax or horsehair until you feel the tent or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no opening for excretion, wind, or air occurs as we have said: you know that it does not penetrate; therefore hurry to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula reaches to the bladder or to the conduit of urine, then he urinates through it, and cannot be cured with medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it reaches to the joint of the thigh, then the swelling comes up to that place; if there is no tortuosity and the pain surrounds it, then it will immediately become a bone abscess, and neither medicine nor treatment by ointment can help; and in these perforated fistulas, there is no cure other than labor, and vanity of foolish physicians who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case that is not perforated and is not old, there is hope for healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies on his back; raise his legs up to his thighs, and incline his thighs towards his belly; then insert a lead probe, or a silver one if there is tortuosity, until you know where the swelling is.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you should put your index finger there, and if it seems that the tissue is pierced; and where you feel between your finger the surface or the flesh, then know that it is perforated; do not treat it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is said everywhere that one can heal some, but this happens rarely; and the help one gives there, is to heat the cautery finely according to the width of the fistula, as was mentioned before; and insert it completely hot into the fistula, until it comes near the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that the unhealthy flesh has been burned, which appears like a feather of a bird; and then cure with moistened bandages in butter, until healthy flesh grows back, then heal with ointment promoting tissue growth and adhesion.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If that cannot be otherwise for him to be healthy; and if the fistula enters, but does not pierce all the way to the root which is at the base, and there is a thick covering of flesh or tissue between the root and the fistula, and you see the fistula through the covering of the heart; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push forward until you reach the head of the fistula, and then apply the cautery afterwards until it reaches the head of the fistula; he will be freed from the fistula, and it will fall out; then clean the rotten flesh which looks like a feather, and leave nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the sinew fails you, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or a dry medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery brings together two good things: it burns the attached flesh and stops the blood and dries up the moisture; then treat with wet cloths in butter or ground substances until the wound discharges pus, and remove the burned flesh from the wound; then treat the wound with hardening ointments that form a scab, and the medicines should be dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes to the deepest part of the fundament, and is distant from the body, pierce it there at the fundament, and investigate it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent and it is between two layers of tissue or muscle, where it is close to piercing, do not proceed without caution and hope, by employing one of the three methods: either cauterize it as we have said, cut it out completely, or if possible, place tents and treat it as described first; but do not go too deep, that you may cut into the tissue holding the fundament, and let evacuation occur naturally as desired; then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will heal, or remove the covering when it has been cut near the fundament, either by tenting or with another appropriate instrument; then clean the infected flesh in the wound as much as possible; then work to restore the wound and keep the fistula outside of the fundament: this will be a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes there are fistulas in this manner: and when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is at the depth of the foundation near the skin above, take a probe perforated at the tip according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And twist the thread in place, and insert the probe along the entire length of the thread into the fistula until it reaches the tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it penetrates the margin of the foundation inside, then withdraw the thread from that passage, so you insert your finger into the foundation; and pull the tip of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and hold them tight to each other, and leave it for one or two days; and tighten it at times, until the thread cuts through the tissue between them and they heal; then treat the wound until it is sealed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not rupture, pierce it in all ways that you can, if it is not too hard.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to operate on it if it is too hard, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spinous process where one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and not so on the other, because one must not cut what should not be cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	for hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: those that are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they contain blood. There can be one or several, and some are near the anus while others are at its head; but those further away have less moisture, and still have a little yellow water or blood, and their color matches the skin. The treatment for those inside the anus is that you instruct the patient to strain to expel them until they protrude from the anus; then, quickly grasp them with forceps at your fingernail, cut off at their roots; if the forceps cannot hold due to moisture, use a piece of cloth or cotton instead. Pull out with both hands, then cut and apply warm cautery powders suitable for cauterization as described in the chapter on cautery, then treat them further until they heal. If the anus does not protrude, administer an astringent enema to wash what is inside the anus so it can be expelled freely; when the patient strains, if the filaments have come out of the anus, the treatment is easier. Grasp them with your fingernail or forceps and cut them off, then treat as previously described until healed, and beware of iron incision.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So you must treat the suture in this manner: take twisted thread and put it on a needle, then pull the thread from above and pierce the needle from another part, and turn both ends of the thread under the needle, and let it be wide; then tighten the thread completely, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and do so for all others, and leave one to drain excess blood; then place a base piece of moistened linen in rose oil or cerate, and place the base, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave it until they excrete, and when they have passed, treat them with ointment and other treatments, until they are healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the dryness of the feces at the base
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is dryness of phlegm in the intestines, and by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should cut with the tip of a scalpel or your nail through the skin above it, without letting it moisten; then treat it until it is dry as needed; and if it cannot be dried, shave it more forcefully than before, until it bleeds much and is skinned; then treat it until it heals.
dou fremit	with tremor
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A flea bite is a small reddish mark on the body, and it stings very sharply; and sometimes it causes coldness, and one feels it like death by tremor, and it spreads throughout the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take a quill from a goose's feather or a strong vulture's feather, and place this quill over the tumor, so that the circles perfectly encircle the tumor; then turn your hand around the whole quill until you have circled the entire tumor, and apply it firmly, and scrape the tumor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a wire of iron or steel according to this form, and let it be fine below and drawn above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, to hold the hair in place and press the hair And if you wish, cauterize the tumor as described earlier in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes a enema is made of silver or sorrel, or of melted silk or barley; and sometimes these instruments are made small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are treated in the care of children and those who are weak and in pain are given small ones.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large enema is as follows, wide, and the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there should be a space where the belly is bound as you see, and the end through which it is inserted should be pierced; and on one side have two holes, and on the other one hole; and let the belly in which the medicine is placed be made of an animal bladder or parchment, and pierce it all around with small holes, and leave a space of one finger between each hole, then insert a strong cord through these holes twisted ten times or more, and secure the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread, then administer the enema; this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with a mixture of oil or duck egg, or similar thing, then pour it on gently; then press the patient's temples with both hands, until he is fully covered, then remove the mixture, and lift the patient's legs to the wall, and if the medicine wishes to come out, let him hold back as long as he can; and if he sleeps a whole night straight, so much greater help will be received.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give an enema in the case of diarrhea and the medicine wishes to come out quickly, then repeat it until he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the fundament or abscess, then let the enema be as fine as for a child; and this is the form of a fine enema in which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments with hands and medicines, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds vary according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are from falling stones, and cuts from swords and knives, or lances or staffs or arrows, or similar objects; and they are made according to the places on the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or on the foot, or on the belly, or on the liver, and other limbs; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will start with simple head wounds, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from falling of stones or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound large, and you suspect formation of a hot abscess: then I treat it immediately with cephalic cautery if little blood flows from the wound, and let the dressing be contrary to the wounded part; and prevent the patient from overeating wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to be cauterized, then reduce his flesh and let him drink no wine or eat meat; and place on the wound, if hot abscesses are coming, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then apply to the fresh wound that has not been exposed to air, powder which I will describe a little later; and if it has become inflamed by exposure to air, then apply some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar ones, and the lips cannot be brought together by tenting, then sew them together as I will explain for belly wounds, of the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed bone, and if it can be done without causing further harm to only a small part, then cut it out; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat hearty foods, such as brains and cooked wheat, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrefaction in the skin that does not adhere to the bone, cut out all the rotten flesh and expose it to air, then treat it; and if there is an artery or vein in the wound that cannot be staunched with medicine, tie off the artery; and if you find it dislocated, ligature it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: it is that you put in this powder which adheres as though the burn has healed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live charcoal three parts, and finely powder them, and apply to the wound, and press firmly until it adheres well and joins with all its blood; then bind it tightly, and do not loosen unless it swells; for the medicine should not be removed until it is healed.
