Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one uses charcoal alone when there is no incense or dragon's blood available, but the burn has not healed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved or changed, especially in summer, do not apply this powder; but use some digestible ointments, or a poultice made of barley flour with water and honey, until it discharges fluid; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of a bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you hereafter about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference from that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is severed.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, then there should be no other treatment but to leave it alone and not put anything constricting on it, for it harms the nerves and makes them retreat; and do not apply anything cold to the wound, as the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as hot water mixed with sweet water, and rose oil, and linen cloth washed in sweet water, and other minerals according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then stitch and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and swollen with pus, then pierce it at its lowest part; and if an artery is cut and bleeding occurs, then open it, tie it off, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut or the windpipe is damaged, through which flesh passes, sew the wound over the windpipe but do not touch the throat, rather set it according to its natural form; and then bind it properly, and leave it for a few days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then probe it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove them all if you can, and those that you cannot have, let remain as long as the wound suppurates, and be separated and eased the exit; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is an abscess, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a lance or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or knife and the wound is deep, then look to see if the wound spouts windiness which the patient belches: you will then know that the wound is fatal; but if it is not deep and fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder at the first hour, nor bind it for the blood that does not pour deeply, lest it return to the heart and kill the patient; instead, use a drawing ointment, and bandage twice daily. And if you have no ointment, place old cotton in the wound to absorb fluid outside moisture, and let the patient rest on the wound three days, or four, or more; thus spasm, nor trembling, nor heart malady strangulation will not occur; and when you see good signs, then know that the wound is safe.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it then with tents and other treatments until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, and you operate, then you know that there is an abscess; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, whether on the front or back, treat it as such; if it is large, stitch it up; if it is small, apply powder; and if it is pressed against the bone with pieces broken off, clean the wound, and draw out any separated tendons; and if they are not separated, let the wound heal by itself, which will ease the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, judgment should be as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	from the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the abdomen is great and medium and small; from the large wound sometimes the intestines come out, or the nerves of the intestines, due to which there is an infection; and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a larger one because when you replace the intestines less often they can go back in further, as soon as they feel cold, they retract more tightly, and thus it becomes necessary to move the medium-sized wound's intestines back to their place that others do not; and know that the rupture of the abdomen happens according to four ways: two common sutures occur with the suture of the abdomen, and the suturing of other wounds of the body are two other proper ones for the abdomen; yet they are more specifically related to abdominal sutures, and I will tell each one and clarify them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine protrudes, it is a difficult thing to replace, which can be done by one of two methods: either because of the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a piece of cloth with hot water only, which you cook in water scented with cypress and spikenard, and rinse the intestines until the swelling subsides; and sometimes use wine that restrains, and it should be prepared to help reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling begin to subside, moisten the intestines with water in which hellebore and mallows have been cooked, for this helps gradually open the entry; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment should be such that one does not need to cut unless there is great necessity; and here is the instrument for making the incision: cut inwardly along the curvature and do not go outward, as shown in this form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines protrude outward, place them back in their natural form in their proper place if you have the power to do so, for it is better that way.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the back part of the abdomen, you must make the patient lie on his back, with his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the front part of the abdomen, raise the head and feet higher than the middle parts; and similarly, if there is a rupture in one of the two sides, elevate the injured side higher than the other; and thus you should treat large and medium wounds as I have described.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, place what is appropriate for it, then hold a minister who can cover the entire wound with their hand and bring together the edges; this is the common method of suturing. Take one or more needles according to the width of the wound, leaving an inch from the edge of the wound, and insert a needle with strong thread in it; pierce both sides of the skin with the two points inside the skin until you perforate that part, and bring together the four points; then strain a double thread around the needle on both sides, and join the two sides of the wound gradually, leaving another inch space and inserting another needle; tie the knot of the thread as you did for the first needle, and continue doing this according to how many needles you need until the entire wound is closed. The needles should be medium-sized, between fine and coarse, because too fine needles cut through all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot enter properly: they should therefore be medium-sized; it is also not advisable to insert the needles too far from the flesh and skin, as they may damage the wound before suturing; then trim the ends of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient when sleeping, and put tents or cloth at the end of the needles to hold them in place until the wound heals. This method of sewing with needles is more suitable for small wounds. The second suture technique involves bringing together both sides of the skin and the two points inside the skin with one needle or a medium-strong thread; when you have pierced these four points, rethread the needle at the part where you started in the manner that cloth is sewn; leave an inch space between each stitch. This method is known to people, and I sutured a wound on a man's abdomen, which was cut by a knife, about one handspan wide, with intestines protruding two handspans out, located in the middle of his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to him after it had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound was sealed up until fifteen days, and I treated him, and he was well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was well.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing: take the needle, and bring it from the outer part to the inner; when it has pierced the skin straight through, lay the head of the suture where you have inserted the needle, and make it pierce again from the inner part outwards; and the understanding of this suture is that you sew as tailors do with fur, and leave once the suture on one side, and take it up on the other, until the entire seam is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, which Galen describes precisely, is as follows: one brings together the two parts naturally and applies one end of the suture to the other end in this manner: insert a needle at the nearest point on the margin, piercing only that spot, leaving the two ends of the suture; then turn the needle, and pierce from the outer part to the inner part, through the two ends of the suture; then pierce one and the other from the outer part to the inner part, in two points on the opposite side at the margin; and this is the simpler method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this, and some witness it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, each having thread; and one should insert one needle from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew belts; and know that when the rupture is inside the belly, the suturing is more difficult than for other areas of the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is like the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as if the flesh has been burned off, then replace the intestines and sew them; then put on a powder to heal flesh, and if the flesh has been burned off, put on any ointment that is present until the wound heals; then stitch the wound as you do for others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, then put on old cotton as soon as it begins to discharge pus, twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will affect the principal limbs, then it is necessary to moisten light wool in warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the angles and under the armpits; and if there is pain or putrefaction in the bowels, which often happens, then give a clyster of boiled black wine, especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestines; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it heals more easily than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is pierced, and this is due to the smallness of its veins that are there, and the subtlety of all the body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the spleen jumps out of the wound, put it back in as you would with the intestine while it is fresh; and if it has become old and turned black or dark, then tie off the area that is black so that no more blood flows there, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligament, and let both ends hang from below the wound up to where it falls when the spleen drops out, and the wound will heal.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the eye
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is punctured and the wound is small, it can sometimes be restored in some people, as I witnessed a man who was pierced in the abdomen with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and developed into a fistula, from which excretion and flatulence emerged; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not stop suturing until he was healed, and the flesh sealed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it seal, I feared the patient might have pain in his abdomen; but he had no pain, and remained in better conditions, eating and drinking; and some experienced practitioners said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be treated in this manner: take clamps with large heads, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the clamp opens its mouth, place it on both lips so that they grip tightly; then cut off the head, and it stays such that it cannot be loosened, then put another clamp after in the same way as before, until the entire wound is covered; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the head is embedded in the intestine and causes no harm to the patient, one can sew the intestine with a fine thread that matches the intestine of an animal as follows: take the tip of this intestinal thread and make it very clean, then twist a thin linen thread around the tip, put the thread on a needle, and sew the intestine back together; and this method of stitching is not wrong according to trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the main intestinal areas, there is no remedy or treatment except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it begins to heal, is generally called a "fistula," especially when it becomes hollow and reenters the body.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth an abnormal knot hard and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also hair-like as a bird's feather; and sometimes it appears clear pus, and other times thick; sometimes it is little, and other times enough; and I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is none other than by one of the IX causes: namely, due to the thinness of blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the edges, where it does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is rotten, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine used in treatment is not good; or due to corruption being similar to plague; or due to the nature of the region having late digestion, and late healing, and swollen by nature; or it has veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the remedies with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I shall make known to you the treatment of a fistula which is performed by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You should know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or on the surface, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in some ribs, or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet; and some affect the principal part of the limb and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is no remedy but labor, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach the places I have mentioned, and you have confidence in the treatment, and want to know it, take a probe of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, and insert it; and if the fistula is curved, search it with a fine probe made of lead, because lead can bend around the curvature; and if the fistula has several openings and you cannot properly examine it with probes, then clisterize through one of its openings, as moisture flows from one opening to another, and cleanse it; then gently feel carefully with your hand, to know if there is bone or nerve, and whether it is covered by flesh, and ask the patient well about the pain they feel when you press your hand, and where they feel it; and once you truly know where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, a nerve, an artery, or a vein, or in any of the places I have told you, then cut according to what I have said, and remove the unhealthy matter that is inside; and then heal until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep straight ahead, you must cut deeply as much as possible, then place wet probes in medicinal astringent, and push them up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; and then apply healing ointments to regenerate flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this method, cauterize as we have said, and if the bone has been corrupted by the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or artery does not distress the principal limbs as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is putrefaction and blackening, then cut away until all the putrefaction is removed, then treat with remedies to heal flesh until it is sound; and if it is not sound, and you go deep as before, know that you are not yet at the bottom: uncover and search until you reach the bottom, remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus sound, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If that is not the case, know that the corruption is too deep to reach; there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature; and if there is a small corrupted bone that you can pull with forceps, then extract it with an appropriate instrument, and if there are many bones, pull them all out without leaving even one; and if the moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cut through both flesh and bone, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, place on the wound something that promotes putrefaction, and leave it until the flesh around the bones is rotten, then at that time the bones will have more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as from a leg or thigh, reduce only the corruption so that all blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is much of the corrupt part, reaching to the marrow of the bone; you must cut out and scrape everything up to the corruption, and then treat it until it heals; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something that entered his body, such that the matter came to his leg and it swelled with an abscess, and there was no reason for pus to escape by opening; but the doctors, out of their folly, operated so much on the abscess until they opened it, and they removed a great deal of matter from it, and it became a fistula, and many holes appeared through which all flesh and body moisture leaked; and many doctors treated him for two years, and no one showed any skill in the art of hands, until I was called to see him, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what came out from the holes as great bodies; and the skin of the young man turned red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that they came together from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the holes until I discovered part of the bone, which was corrupted and perforated; and the corruption extended to the inner part of the bone. I cleansed what appeared to be the corrupted bone and believed there was no further corruption beyond what I had removed. I began to treat the wound with internal medicines over a long period, but it could not heal properly. Then I started again, cut into the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone; I cleansed it and then removed it, and tried to close the place; however, I was unable to do so until I cut around one palm's width of the bone and treated it entirely with medicines. It healed quickly and closed properly, but no further work needed to be done except for the patient's weakness, which could not bear more, and out of my fear of death for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often there was an evacuation of blood, but he remained entirely healthy, and in place of the bone grew a hard flesh, and he had good health and suffered no harm or contrary effect, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated as follows: take some linen and stretch it over the end of the visible bone, and have someone extend it upward; then place another piece of coarser linen underneath the skin near the bone, and tie it so that you pull the corrupted flesh inward, exposing the healthy flesh where you wish to treat it, ensuring that the bandage does not irritate the flesh; and put a cautery stick or plate under the bone to cut away the corrupted flesh; and continue treating until one can see and feel that all corruption is gone, and treat again if necessary.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and it does not appear clearly, and the corruption is in the middle or a part of it, then uncover all the flesh; then place an ember underneath, and then apply thread from one side to the other along the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut off the corrupted joint and sew up the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is at the continuation of two joints, there is no other remedy but cutting; and if the corruption is in the thumb of the hand or foot, it is very severe, but nevertheless you must investigate this corrosion as it appears to you; and cleanse it in all possible ways, but do not let veins or nerves obstruct you; and know that instruments for incision and sewing up these bones are many according to the structure of the bones, their appearance, thickness and fineness, size and smallness, hardness; therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument suitable for each kind of work; and know that your work will show you what tool you need based on the knowledge of this art and evidence from the ways diseases manifest; so consider the tool you need according to what is required.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head may rot inwardly or outwardly; and when you have treated that corruption with the medicine, and it is of no benefit, then it is necessary to amputate that limb up to where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes from this death, or from the greater evil of losing the limb; and the signs are that the limb turns black, as if it were burned by fire, and rots afterwards, for the corruption spreads from member to member, and takes over the whole body; therefore hasten to amputate, and if this is due to the bite of venomous animals, such as sea scorpion and viper and similar, and the corruption is at the top of the head, then cut it off, and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cut at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut with a knife; and if it passes the knife, it is death, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of its virtue; and do exactly this when the corruption comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, cut after the next joint; and if it reaches the foot, cut all the way through the foot; and if it rises up to the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or sawing the limb is that you tie it from top to bottom, and one minister holds down one end, and another minister holds up the other end, and you separate the flesh which is between the two ends by a width of one span, until the bone is exposed; then cut or saw, and place a strip of linen on each side so that the cut does not touch healthy skin and cause another injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you treat it, cauterize the area quickly or apply some constricting powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the affected limb with an appropriate bandage and continue treatment until he is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in such a case: a black spot appeared on his foot which seemed like a burn from fire, and this corrosion spread first in his heel of the foot, spreading throughout the entire foot; when the man saw the corrosion, he hurried to amputate his foot and was healed; some time after, the corrosion returned at the heel of his hand, and he came to me, and I applied counteracting substances after cleansing his body, but could not stop the corrosion; he asked that I cut off his hand, and I refused because I had hope in countering the matter; also feared that if I cut his hand, he might die, for his strength was weak; and he despaired entirely, returned to his homeland, hurriedly amputated his hand, and was healed; except for this case of doing differently when it is necessary, I have no other content to relate.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess appears in the flesh and remains so long that it gathers much pus; then it bursts and drains, leaving a wound like a vase; and the skin above is as thin as delicate cloth, not reaching to the bone or the nerve, and such sickness is called "saint," and is not called "fistula"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone deeply, it is called "fistula"; and the skin must be cut all around when it is thin, just like cloth; and it does not heal because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you trust that the skin will heal and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, cure it by clistering thus: look to see if the breast is swollen, and the pus coming from it has a foul odor, then clisterize it with Egyptian medicine which is made as follows: take wax, oil, and litharge equally, and heat them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take what you need according to your necessity, mix it with water and honey, and use it to clisterize the breast while restraining the passage; leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by straining; do this many times, until the breast is cleansed and the foulness removed; sometimes when Egyptian medicine or water from ashes is not available, clisterize with water mixed with a little litharge powder, ground up; or you can clisterize with honey and vinegar, where the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine helps to heal; once this is done and you believe the breast is well cleansed, then clisterize it with something that causes flesh to grow, such as a diaphoretic ointment made with rose oil and in wine; or use some medicine and ointments whose properties I have described when treating ointments; if the opening of the breast is small, and the tube for clistering cannot enter, then enlarge it slightly with an iron tool and place on a dressing of Egyptian ointment or basilicon until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, sew it up so only one spot where the clister can enter remains, and if the pus-draining opening is above this point, cut below that area.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the wound is deep, it does not allow flesh to grow; and if you cannot cut the breast below as you wish, prepare it in such a way that the pus flows downward to the lowest place where it is; for when the wound is deep, it does not allow flesh to grow and if you cannot cut the breast below as you wish, prepare it in this manner: so that the pus runs gently down, and leave nothing of the pus behind; then take consolidating medicines to apply on the wound, and stretch a linen cloth covering all the wound; then cut slightly larger than the first hole at the force points of the chest; then place another piece of cloth according to the size of the hole, and put it over the hole in the wound to ease the pus out, and do not remove the large cloth outside until after several days once; and that which is on the hole of the breast, remove often to take out the pus, and check what comes from the pus, whether it is venomous or somewhat or enough, or digested or undigested; and be cautious if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine is applied in this manner and you see the nature that jumps over the hole of the wound, then check that the wound begins to heal, and approach health; and then loosen it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you loosen the wound, change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the stomach throws up undigested food after many days, know that the stomach does not settle.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons come after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are those to whom healing of flesh in their wounds is delayed, and others who do the opposite; and if undigested food vomits from the stomach after many days, know that the stomach does not settle; and if the stomach delays in digesting and is distended, add medicines that are dry in substance but moist in virtue, such as a diaphoretic ointment, for it contains much vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take a diaphoretic ointment, which is made with rose oil, and rinse it with equal parts of old wine; then boil it down and use it; and the same is better when thickened, if a diaphoretic ointment is not present, or you take mastic, aloes, and incense, and grind them, and powder them over honey that is on the fire; then glue a piece of cloth to it and apply it to the stomach; sometimes administer aristolochia longa, and roots of celestial lily, which are like fine flour of fennel and centaury; use simple or compound remedies: grind them, make powder, mix with the honey as I have said, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and not cured by this remedy, then know that corruption is deep-seated, and affects the bone, or hard parts, or ligaments; treat it according to the treatment of fistula as we have mentioned before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panaritis is an abscess that arises from beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or occasionally on other joints; and when it grows old, and no attention is paid to it, a foul abscess comes, running and discharging pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps runs entirely around it; and corrosion comes up to the bone, causing putrid pain, and the finger head becomes swollen, and the color changes.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the section, and the treatment does no good, then it is necessary that you cut away all the excess that remains from the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great aid if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the flesh, and it begins to hurt, and becomes swollen, then you must place the blade under the nail that hurts the flesh, and push it up, and cut away that flesh carefully and gently, and apply the rest of the flesh with burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it out and pull forth, for as long as the bone remains corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see that the part is corrupted, then cut it out as previously described, then treat it until it heals; and if it is pierced and there is great pain, then first you must heal it; then carefully cut off the nail diagonally with a sharp blade, and be careful not to cut into the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, place something on it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the stiffness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The second joint that is born in the hands of some people by chance is all flesh, and sometimes it has bones, and at times there is a nail, and some of them are born at the root of the joint, where the origin is in some places among the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born with any part of the finger missing do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the finger may sometimes move; the size of the one that is all flesh is so slight, in this manner: measure it from its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born at the root of the joint are difficult to treat: be careful when cutting them.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In one who is born or should be at the back side, you must first cut away the flesh roundly until reaching the bone, then cut the bone in one stroke appropriately for that person, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The union that comes to the two together happens by birth, or by joining of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You must cut away that union so that the bones repair according to their natural forms; then place between two cloths or wet bandages in rose oil so they do not unite again; or you may place between two pieces of fine wax until the wound is healed as required.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a union occurs with one of the bones along with the palm, you must cut away that union as required.
des vils	of worms
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are thick and enveloped, full of melancholic excesses, which occur in many parts of the body; and more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer enemas at times, and then treat them with basilicon ointment.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is according to two methods: one is that you cut and draw out the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The treatment by venesection is as follows: first apply a hot water poultice to the leg very strongly until the thick blood becomes thin, then lift the patient's leg from above the thigh down to below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two or three places, making a wide incision, and then hold it open and draw out the black blood with your hand from one side to the other, as much blood as the patient can withstand; then bandage it, and instruct him to abstain from food that produces black bile; and repeat the evacuation and treatment when the veins are full, and do not harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The elevation of the vein is done in this manner: raise the patient's leg if it has much hair, then place it in a bath, and wash the leg with hot water until it becomes red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, warm it by the fire, and then cut along the vein from the ankle to the top of the knee, or above the part below the ankle; then work the skin with an oncine (sharp instrument), and strip the vein on each side until it feels sharp when touched; and it appears red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then raise the edge underneath, and then smooth it lightly with the oncine as you have done before; then cut another incision, or several if needed, then lift it up, and cut at the toe joint, then draw and lift until reaching the second incision; then draw out from one incision to another until it comes out completely, then cut it off; and if you cannot draw it out and lift it, insert a needle through the entire strong double thread, tie it and pull, and place a rod underneath, turning your hand from side to side until it is done; and beware that it does not break, for if it breaks, it cannot be drawn or lifted, which causes harm to the patient; and when you have completely treated it, put linen soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound site; then cure it until he is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it sharply, but do not cut it off; and draw it out as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which the vein is cut is curved, and it does not slice, so as to cut the vein; and it is thickly curved, because if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry ground with little moisture; and perhaps it may arise elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to putrefaction that comes beneath the skin, as it arises within the body like serpents and worms, lying between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there comes a very great inflammation in the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to come out, as if it were the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein is open, you must wrap around a piece of linen from one and a half to two fingers wide, tie it, and leave the linen hanging down the leg. Every time it comes loose, rewrap it around the linen and tie it; if it is too long, cut off part of it, but do not cut it at its root until it is entirely out, for cutting it will make it go back into the flesh, causing abscesses and putrefaction in that place, and a serious illness. Therefore, treat this vein slowly over time until nothing remains in the body; sometimes this vein can be five or ten palms long when treated, and once I had a patient whose vein was twenty fingers long when it came out. When you cut off one finger-width of it, pierce it to its core so that everything comes out; empty the matter inside, and then apply medicines against putrefaction for some days, then treat it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein is deeper, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot, or in the foot itself, and there are many perforations, and thus it bleeds profusely; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "disease of the ox," because it often affects oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body moving up and down, and one feels it well as it moves from limb to limb, until it breaks through the skin where it goes, causing pain; and it is engendered by putridity of certain humors, just as worms, serpents, lice, and ascarids come from the belly; and one fears its malice, because when it travels through the body, and ascends to the head, and comes to the eye, perhaps it enters there and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see that it needs to be drained and drawn out, one cannot do so except when it goes: therefore you must tie the place above and below with a strong cord tightly, then cut over it and draw it out forcefully; and if the pus is deep in the flesh, and you do not find it, cauterize with fire until it stops; and the greatest harm that it causes is that it may corrode the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the eye on top, then tightly hold below the eyebrow, then cut over it, and draw it out forcefully; and the patient must use cleansing of body with medicines dissolving bad humors and refrain from food causing putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen those whom I tell you about.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, where I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise as fast as a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, like quicksilver when it flows from one place to another; the pain departed from that spot and fixed itself in the shoulder, and then a short while later ran through the entire body until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it kept circling around her body quickly as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved limb by limb, for I had never seen this disease in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had heard of many who had wished to move pain from one place to another, but I had not seen it as such, just as I saw in the woman; and I thought that this was because the woman had a dry body, and veins exposed, and for this reason wind appeared constrained; and it does not appear according to this reasoning with those who are plump, and who have moist bodies and hidden veins.
