Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you wish to treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if she shows it as we have said, lift up above and below quickly, and then incise where that wind is constrained; and cauterize that place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, cure it by those who expel winds, such as fetid pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse according to their appearances and the places in the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of arrows is such that there are those with large points, small points, barbed points, and fixed points; and those with two angles, and some with tongues, and others with pieces; and when an arrow strikes any limb, it does so in two manners: either striking a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, stomach, spleen, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it strikes any part of these members and the signs of death, which I will tell you next, become apparent: then you must be wary about extracting this arrow, for death often follows in many cases; and when none of these bad signs appear and the arrow is not deeply embedded, remove it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the brain when an arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and passes through the dura mater which is over the brain, are scotoma and stiffness and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasm and impairment of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and sometimes it issues without strength from the nostrils or ears; and by chance speech and voice are lost; and from the wound flows white moisture like pus, and also like blood serum; and if these signs appear to you, then hold off on treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is within.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the arrow when it strikes the heart are that it is near the left mammary region, and feels as if it were embedded in something hard, not empty; and by chance the arrow moves like pus, and black blood flows, and coldness and cold sweat come, and syncope occurs: you then know without doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that wounds the abdomen is that without a flow of pus it bubbles from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes in the cover of the hip, it is near the small ribs; and there is much pain and great suffering and sighing; and all the shoulder members move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes in the stomach, it may bubble up from the wound some undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes in the belly, and no sign of it can be found through the intestines all the way, there is no hope for treatment, nor for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes leaking, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and arm and spine of the back and forearm and thigh and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, for that reason you should act differently.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell into his helmet at the root of his nose: I felt it, and drew it out from the other side under the fat of the ear, and he was safe without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And he pulled out an arrow that stuck in the fat under the eye below the eyelid, and the arrow was embedded, and only the tip towards the shaft could be reached, and the arrow was large for a Turkish bow, made entirely of light iron without ears; the man was healthy, and no bad accidents happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And he pulled an arrow out of the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears; I held the beard points, and carefully pulled until it came out, and the Christian was healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And he pulled an arrow out of the man who had it lodged in his stomach, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days had passed, there was no change in his condition; I incised around the arrow, probed it, forcefully extracted it, and no bad accidents occurred.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to treat a man who has an arrow embedded in his back, and the wound is sealed over; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change his natural disposition, nor finds harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you wish to treat another man who has an arrow embedded in his face, and the wound is sealed over; and it remains thus without him suffering great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated an arrow for the king's prince, which was embedded in his nose, and it was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was completely bent. I was called to treat it three days after it had entered.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I asked for it to be placed in a very fine tent, and I felt nothing; but he felt pricking and pain behind his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I placed a plaster with drawing and digestive properties there so that the area would not swell; and I saw the place where the arrow had been.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on for several days, and reopened the wound again, and the patient remained this way for a long time until he felt the arrow one day in his nose; and then he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was open, and I examined it, feeling the tip of the arrow that was lodged there; then I continued to work around the opening with this corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow became visible. It took about four months before I could clearly see the end of the shaft. Then I widened the wound so much that I could place pliers into it and tried to extract it from both sides, but it would not come out; then I did not stop trying various instruments in subtle ways until one day I managed to grasp it with well-made pliers according to what is described at the end of this chapter, and pulled it out, restoring the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physician judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I then repaired it, and the wound was sealed, and the patient was entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you about the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you do not focus on what I do not say, for books cannot contain everything; but wise masters compare well and understand much, and upon what is present and lacking, they find new work, and new instruments, in descending from things strange which happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows exit from the limbs where they are lodged in two ways: either through the place where they entered, or through another part; and those that come out through the place where they entered, these are penetrating arrows, and sometimes they come out immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, leave it until the flesh around it is ripe and the opening enlarged; and likewise if it is fixed in the bone, and cannot be removed, leave it thus for several days, and soften it each day; then it will come out, and if it still does not come out, pierce around it with a very fine point, until the flesh around it is expanded, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head and reaches one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents I have mentioned become apparent to the patient: do not extract it, but leave it for several days until it becomes even, because if the arrow reaches the membrane, death will follow.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is embedded only in the bone and does not reach the surface, and the patient remains for some days without any adverse incident, then attempt to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, administer warm applications around it, as I have told you; then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in a place where it cannot be seen, search throughout the body for it; and if you feel it, extract it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound or the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins nearby, enlarge the wound until it is large enough; and extract the arrow if possible, and if the arrow has barbs that hold it in place, remove the flesh around them from both sides as much as you can, and then bend or break the barbs so that you may pull out the arrow; be careful not to break the arrow shaft, which would make extracting it more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the area around the site is prepared, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes it difficult, follow what we have said about treatment in its chapter; and beware of cutting into the nerve and vein, and position the arrow so you can safely remove it, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient as he was when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot, then follow what the signs indicate to you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where it leaves some sign of itself, or the skin is swollen in such a way that it can be seen or felt clearly: cut then above it until the forceps can grasp it, and then extract it: do this now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand around until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it there and then try the extraction again until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is still inside, push it along the entire shaft; and if the shaft breaks off, and you wish to administer a probe, apply an instrument with a head so that the point of the arrow enters into the head of the instrument; and then push firmly, and if the arrowhead is separated, insert the instrument with a pointed end to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is contaminated, it is necessary that you cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if possible, then treat the wound as required.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls on the foot or in the belly or bladder or chest, and it is close to the surface, then cut over it if you can; be careful not to cut the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound if necessary; continue treating it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the hair needle is also like the feather of a bird, to push at the tip of the arrow, as shown here is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the tongs for inserting and grasping is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins from which one can bleed for treatment, sixteen of which are in the head: two beating veins behind the ears, called "herbech"; and the two arteries visible in the temples; and the two veins under the eyebrows above each eye, called "aspires"; and the vein across the forehead; and the vein on top of the nose; and the two jugular veins in the neck; and the two veins in the upper lips, which are called "augeherich"; and the two veins beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one usually draws blood are four in each arm: the first is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side, and the lay people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "faste," and it consists of the cephalic and basilic veins, and the lay people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and they call it the "vein of the belly" by the lay people, and it is above the fosse, and this one from which blood is usually drawn, appears clearly over the pouchet.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and on the foot are three veins: one is below the curve of the pocket on the left side, and the second sophene which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called "nesse," which is at the other ankle; and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloodletting from the veins that are behind the ears helps with chronic catarrhs and migraines; and the quality of this bloodletting, as I tell you, is that you bend the patient's head back, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient’s neck with a strap so that the two veins become visible behind the ears: grasp them with your thumb, and at the spot where you feel the pulse below your thumb, incise there; then take the lancet and pierce just under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire length of the vein, cutting both the skin and the vein cleanly twice the width of the vein, and let out as much blood as you wish; then tie it off and bandage it until it is healed; and I have already mentioned incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bloodletting of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for chronic headaches and severe migraines, and for habitual ophthalmia with excessive tears in the eyes; and the qualities of this bloodletting are as follows: The patient should hold their neck tightly so that both veins appear clearly; then feel the pulse under your finger, and then cut above it; lift the hand over the vein at the top of the arm, place the lancet underneath, raise the vein up, and incise it as you did with the other two veins, allowing blood to flow according to necessity; then release the patient, placing a cloth on the arm for an hour, then put cotton on it; then dress the wound properly, leaving it until it is healed; we have already spoken about their coating and extraction at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The vein of the forehead is worth as much as the cephalic vein for ancient face diseases and for migraines and redness; and its quality is that the patient strains his neck by twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "digger", which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you wish; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is secure, and sometimes wrap it in a wide bandage.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not appropriate for the bandages to be too tight; and apply them diagonally, because the bone is nearby, and by chance they might break if they are delicate.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bloodletting from the two veins that are in the two grooves helps with the eyes, and for tinea, and for redness, and for cataracts in the eye, and for diseases of the face; and the quality of their bloodletting is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting some kind of ligature as before; then let the blood flow, and may the incision be straight, a little long of flame a little wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flammable part is fine, it may break; then let the blood flow, as much as you need, and then bandage it with cloth, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bloodletting from the vein of the nose is good for fever, and for violent diarrhea, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, especially when it is old; and the quality of this bloodletting is that the patient strains his neck, then strangles his nose with your left hand, and take a fine long flame, and insert it between the lips in the space which is between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well inwardly, and the blood will now begin to flow; and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bandage it for one night, because it heals very quickly; and this is the form of the incision:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The salve of the two binders helps in the constriction of the wound, and at the beginning of mixing, and for many diseases, and for empetigo, and corrosives, and herpes, and eschars; and the qualities of the salve are such that the patient constricts his neck under each one as we have said; and let the masters being on the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair, then apply the vein of the long somewhat broadly, then draw blood moderately, or as much as is needed; then do the same in the other vein, then undo the binding, and moderate all veins so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the salve of the leaves
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The veins of the upper lips inside help against inflammation in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and cracks of lips, and nose and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of this treatment are to have the patient sit before you, and hold his neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by their blackness, and also because around them are small black veins: so cut both of them, and if you do not know them, and you doubt, then cut the larger one on each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	From the sore remove the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The sore of the veins that are behind the tongue is followed by the treatment of the cephalic vein, which is at the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the healer is such that the patient urinates into your hands in front of the sun, and you lift the tongue, and look behind on each side there are two black veins: treat then one and the other, and do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the arm that are commonly treated are treated in two ways: by puncturing with a broad flame-shaped blade or an olive-shaped fine blade like cutting knives, and it is called "anesil"; and they are wide and fine according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame of fire is much renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open veins that are full of thick, visible blood, and which contain thick, turbid blood; and this is the form of the olive-colored flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is finer and more pointed, and is used to treat fine veins, where there is fine yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps in treating diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the abdomen; and it is necessary for the healer to bleed cautiously, and to be careful not to cut into the artery that lies beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and bleeding occurs, it must be stopped as I have said; and it should not be pricking at the flame, but cutting as before.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein does not appear clearly, then you must extract it and change to another one; where you wish some ligature of it, or you open in its place a vein in the arm: it appears clearly; and cut with the flame as before, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to determine the site of the incision, then it is necessary that you extract the arm, touch the spot until you feel the pulse; then mark the joint location, and tie the arm, and cut the vein with the flame as before; be careful not to injure the artery when you see the area swollen, for this is due to the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it flow upwards like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood: hurry then, and place your hand on it for a long time, then remove your hand if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; be afraid and do not move them until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped, and it becomes necessary, and no medicine is present, then cut the artery if it appears open, for its end can be found; and stop the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take the bark of fig tree, and cut it, and take one half and bind it on well until the other day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, treat it as we have said with powders that stop blood; and the binding does no harm in many conditions for the small area of the wound, and the strength of the bandage on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein in the middle helps to drain blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the surgeon must take care not to cut too deeply, for if he cuts into the nerve beneath, it will swell and damage the health, and perhaps he cannot heal it; this nerve appears in many people, but if it does not appear in some due to its subtlety, then you should heal it with an instrument called anestrum; and avoid this nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The cephalic vein helps to drain blood from the head and aids the eyes; it should be cut carefully using an olive leaf or myrtle leaf, as this is the safest of all veins, for there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, one must choose the lightest place, and it does no harm if it is necessary to do so the first time, and one can repeat; and perhaps the place swells for some people when done the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the salve is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bleeding is that it is only done to preserve health and to prevent future diseases; and one should bleed in one of the three veins which are in the arm: namely, cephalic, basilic, and median; and it should be done at the beginning of spring, autumn, and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and it should be done on the first or third day after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The physician who treats diseases has no fixed schedule, but must be available by day or night, at all hours and in all seasons; and it is not proper to treat children until they are fourteen years old, nor women carrying a fetus from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	And one should not treat the elderly who have passed sixty years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wishes to be bled, in whatever manner, it is necessary for them to cleanse their intestines with a mild enema if they have much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw harmful substances from the intestines; nor should one bleed someone who is too full of meat, or drunk, whether pregnant or not, or those suffering from dropsy; and it is dangerous to bleed after colic, vomiting, diarrhea, excessive sexual activity, labor, staying up late, or fasting; then thin out the humors if the blood is thick with food, drink, and medicine as you are able; then enter a bath, if nothing prevents it, to thin out the blood; and bleed from an arm vein around midday, as we have said; and guard yourself that day against work, pain, lust, and similar things; and be cheerful, and let the physician be higher than the patient, and stroke the patient's arm two or three times, then loosen the bandage moderately, for if it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow properly; then press the bleeding area with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt; then moisten the lancet tip with a bit of old oil, place your left hand over the vein where you wish to bleed, so that the vein does not become firm and collapse at the puncture.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that behave like strings to the surgeon, and some of them are full of airiness, so when one puts on the flame, it retreats from the flame, and thus cannot open the vein, and in this way, one is at a loss; and if he works the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary that surgeons be cautious about such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is worked on the first time, it is good; if not, then begin again a little below that place quickly, if the area is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the area is swollen and the patient is afraid, let him rest for one or two days, and do not bind his arm: perhaps there will come soft abscesses; nor enter a bath, then resume the bloodletting if it pleases him; and if the opening is small, and the skin cuts finely and you doubt that it will release as much blood as you wish, apply the flame directly to that opening quickly; work for a little while until the area is swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not restart the bleeding, and put a little poultice of oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place the poultice is more soothing than oil; and thus administer the poultice of oil each time you bleed to stop the flow of blood; and likewise make a plaster and apply it when you put it on the area; it gently draws off the blood when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens many times, especially when the bleeding is not strong except on the occasion when the vein opening is small, hurry and put on the area a sponge moistened in warm water and vinegar for a while; and it is necessary that you do this after the blood flows from the vein, and if some dark or green substance remains at the site after several days, it does no harm; and if you wish, apply something of aloes or myrrh dissolved in juice of calamint, mastix, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an abscess and swelling occur at the base of the spine: place your hand there, and if you find the spot soft upon pressing with your hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid placing anything from what we have said above, as it might cut into the artery; but apply a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another method until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw out blood from each according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too warm, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is appropriate for one who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, to make a wider incision, and let the flaps be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and he should be bled less frequently and in small amounts, and this should be done by cutting across, not piercing; and this method of bloodletting saves from blood loss and nerve damage, and is better than long or wide cuts.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body requires bloodletting, it is appropriate to give him moist bread in pomegranate juice; if he is heated, let him drink blood three or four times. And if he has a cold complexion, let him eat moist bread in musé syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after losing a lot of blood, it is necessary for him to drink broth made of meat, and fragrant subtle syrup, and use other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bleed his arm and let blood again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by excessive bleeding, that he lets blood a little at a time according to the quantity of his continuous strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, should let blood seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wishes to be bled from another site should do so on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body which is already heated, and it causes fever; therefore, it is necessary to draw out great quantities of it, and widen the passage until it flows easily; then when you see all the conditions for bleeding are met, and place your hand over the pulse as it heals, so death does not come in its place, and this often happens, when bleeders are negligent; nor should you press hard on it if you wish to loosen the arm and draw out blood a second time, and the passage is closed, but do so gently until the coagulated blood at the vein's opening comes forth, then put some salt that has been dissolved in water on it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not bind it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, do so from the same vein, or from another vein, or from the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is bled in place of the head vein because it is composed appropriately.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of bleeding is that the patient immerses his hand in warm water until it turns red; then bind it moderately so that the veins become prominent, then bleed now through them transversely, not widely or lengthwise; and make the punctures wide, and bleed close to the joint of the hand, and if blood does not flow, immerse the hand again in warm water, and let the blood coagulate in the water until you have enough; and if this is done in summer, do not bathe the hand repeatedly in warm water, for it is more often done in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves nearby.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The treatment of the right hand vein is effective for all diseases of the liver, and this is the method: pull out the vein, and insert it into hot water until the vein appears swollen; if it crosses sideways, and you cut it completely through, do not harm anything; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are entirely bare of flesh underneath, and then put the hand back in hot water if the blood congeals in the wound, and no blood can escape.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as is necessary, apply oil and thread to seal it quickly, and do this for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The treatment of the left hand vein is effective for diseases of the spleen, and do it exactly as I have told you for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sinew of the sophene is valuable for all diseases that are below the body, such as disorders of the belly, retention of urine, disease of the thighs, and old diseases of the legs and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its sinew is such that the patient should put his foot in hot water, and rub on the vein until it softens, and place it above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot there are many tendons; treat it then at the widest tendon, or at the ankle, which is much better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you treat it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are below, and treat it by cutting through as well as in incising; and let the flame be steady.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then place the foot in warm water, and let the vein be properly opened.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the incision fails the first time, then begin again slightly above, for the place is saltish; do not fear hitting a nerve, as we have said, and thus do the same incision on the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The site for the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the foot, and its incision relieves hip pain when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its incision is such that the patient enters a bath, and presses above the ankle four fingers by twisting, for otherwise the vein does not appear; and if it appears, then cut it in all ways you can, and across; and be careful not to shave it, as the site is deep, and it is very responsive to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, apply some salve to the area above the back of the foot and towards the small toe, and be careful of the nerves; let the blood flow as much as you wish, then loosen the bandage, and put on cotton and bind it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	suctions of cupping therapy
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping devices are made of horns, or clay, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: one by drawing blood after puncturing the skin, or without puncturing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping without puncturing is done in two ways: with heat or without heat; and the cupping that involves puncturing and drawing blood is performed on fourteen parts of the body: one over the head; another around the neck; two at each side of the neck; one below the chin; two on the shoulders; two above the kidneys; two on the arms; two on the legs; and two on the ankles; and this cupping does not draw blood, except from small veins scattered throughout the flesh, so it does not weaken a person as does phlebotomy; and it should not be administered with or without heat in any disease caused by excess, until all parts of the body are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if due to the necessity of illness it is necessary to bleed, or by habit, we shall perform this at each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and similarly in every season; for there are those who, when they need bleeding, feel a heavy head; and there are some who experience bloating and redness on their face, and on their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and there are some who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue is swollen, and they spit blood; and there are those who dream, and see by night blood and wounds and deaths and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially at the beginning of the month, we instruct them to bleed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The massage of the temple helps with headaches… that affect the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is instead for the massage of the cephalic area, and those with a cold complexion should not use it, nor those who have catarrh, because it causes them great harm; and therefore neither old people nor those who suffer from cold diseases in their head should use it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who become faint from it should be cautious, and for this reason the cupping should be placed a bit lower to avoid the risk of fainting.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventouse on the neck is for the massage of the head and the basilic area, and it is useful for stiffness in the back, rib fractures, general discomfort, and fullness; but it should be applied gently, because if it holds too firmly, fainting or distress can occur in the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Ventosa applied to the second ribs of the neck is effective for headaches, and for ophthalmia and migraine, and for choking, and for pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in the area of the basilic vein; and you must instruct the practitioner not to press on the artery, so there is no bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Ventosa applied below the chin is effective for mouth diseases, and for gum decay, and similar ailments that are in the mouth; and it is in the area of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventosa applied to the shoulders is effective for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Ventosa applied to the sides is as effective as opening three veins in the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the practitioner not to apply it too deeply, for the area lacks flesh, and it lies close to nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup which is on the rump corresponds to hemorrhoids of the anus, and diseases below it, and it must be large, and made of brass, as it needs to pull well; and perhaps if it were delicate, it would break; and thus it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs draw blood powerfully, as they pull blood from the entire body, and are effective for chronic pain in the thighs, and of the kidneys, and of the bladder, and reset the flows; and they are placed at the two soles, and at the two ankles, and over time they weaken the body and cause fainting in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of placing the suction cup is that you place it first empty, and suck moderately, and apply quickly, and move evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the area red and swollen, and the reddish color of the blood appears; then proceed carefully, and replace the suction cups, and be wary of the condition of the body, for there are those who have tender flesh and clear pores: it is necessary to pierce only once, and make large cuts, and a bit deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to cut twice: the first time to make a path for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to cut a third time; and when we wish to draw blood slowly, we need only do it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish to take much blood, we begin frequently; and if the vein is thick, cut deeply, and let the incision be such that it pierces quickly through, which is necessary for those with thick and hard skin, and who have small pores, that you anoint the places with ventouse oil that is appetizing and dissolving: if it is in summer, of violet oil, or almond oil, or cucumber seed oil; and if it is in winter, of radish oil, or of lily, or chamomile, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take oil of ambergris, or balsam, or anise seed oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person being treated has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be applied, but they should be washed after ventosity with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or china pink water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture should rise from a bath of ash water, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large excesses should rise from old wine, or mulberry water, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar; and it is not proper to treat with ventosity before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath one hour or two; and do not sleep after ventosity, and it is necessary for him to bathe, when he should be treated with ventosity and when he has been treated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware if the person who is to be bled is choleric, and if the blood is too thick and inflamed; then he should take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce in their season, and similar things; and eat young birds, and flesh of turtle doves, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion should take syrup of honey, and spiced wine that is between old and new, and eat doves, and eat young birds and small birds and pigeons; and on the day they will be cupped, they should drink more than they eat; and some people should sometimes be given triacle or nutmeg before cupping, or after, to comfort the principal members; and their blood should be subtle, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed without cutting are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and for gout, and on the belly and the buttocks and the thighs and the hip, because these limbs do not tolerate being cut above them, and it is only done to draw blood from limb to limb as we place them over the breasts when the veins flow; to remove the viscosity that exists in the limb, just as we apply suction cups on the belly and on the buttocks to reduce the swelling; and they alleviate pain when there is a blockage or stone, removing by their attractive power perhaps the obstruction, or dislodging the stone from its place; and thus it acts when placed over the liver and spleen where there is retained wind, and these suction cups are administered empty for sucking only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, such as in cases of pleurisy, and in this way one fills the suction cup with hot water alone or with water in which herbs suitable for that purpose have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping vessel administered with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and on the side there is one small hole, as if to insert a needle, and it should be made of brass, smooth so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle there is a crossbar of brass or iron for placing a candle holder, and they vary in size according to the diseases and age of those who use them; for cupping vessels for children are different from those for the elderly, and for thin people than for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should place this cupping vessel on the limb thus: take the candle of wax or pitch and put it in the cupping vessel across the bar that is inside the cupping vessel, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping vessel to avoid burning the patient; then place the cupping vessel on the limb, and make sure both sides are over the hole we mentioned, so when you want, steam can go out, and remove the cupping vessel; and take the bandage as before, and repeat often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the treatment for pleurisy with cupping, there is no rod or hole, and it is applied only when full of fluid, and is placed on the limb solely; and this is the method:
