Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Cupping glasses are used only on parts where cupping vessels cannot be applied due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and on bare flesh, such as the tongue or nose, and other similar places; and when you find cupping glasses that are in mild fluids and clean without sediment, take them; place them in warm water until they feel familiar and have nothing inside; then let blood from a vein and perform cupping, rub the limb until it turns red, and apply the cupping glasses; and when they are full and fall off, if it is an area where cupping can be applied, do so, because this is very beneficial afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the area with a cushion and then apply cold water, very well, and then press it; and if the bruise appears too close to the body without blood vessels, moisten a piece of linen in cold water and place it on the spot until the bruise is reduced; and if there are multiple bruises, place ground vitriol or gall nuts, and similar things, until they are reduced; or you can put half a pound of peeled beans on the area, let them heat up at the spot, this will stop now; and if you need more remedies, take other blood vessels.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the blood vessels do not want to take in, rub the area with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until the bruise releases some blood, and then place them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will heat up; and when you see that they start to drop, sprinkle a little aloeswood and frankincense powder, or ash, and they will now fall.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it concerns the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know this, dear son, that the foolish doctors fall from this chapter because they have never seen any of the ancient books or read any letters on it; and for this reason science is strange in our land, for I found none good; and I know nothing except by the science of the ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life; and I have clearly described to you in this chapter what it contains, and I have summarized it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the discourse and the chapters where the wise one sets his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to someone, you must hurry to treat the patient from both sides if nothing prevents it, such as weakness of body, children, elderly; or if the time is not very warm, or too cold; and eat cold things, that is to say cold dishes, and meat of birds and kids, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until there is no doubt of a hot abscess, nor spreading of matter in the limb; so return to the first governance that he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that promote thick nutrition, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, head cheese, feet, pork belly, eggs, fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For such nourishment promotes healing and the fracture heals more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and infirm do not heal well according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of very young children; but take care, reset on the broken bone a thick splint that holds and joins the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before; and do not disturb its work, and for this one must nourish with heavy foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the spine, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manners of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes in an oblique direction, and another in a sharpened manner, like the shaft of a writing quill.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each manner has its own treatment and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what memory comes to mind; and a bone fracture is known by the twisting of the limb, and is clearly apparent by swelling, and sounds when pressed with the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture; but it may have twisting, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary to move it with your hand, but place the medicines that follow here, and then press it gently now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes into the bone, and are the two parts disjointed, they must now be set equally, so that if there are hot abscesses, you leave it for some days until the abscess is appeased; then you can set it gently and carefully when it has calmed down; know that the restoration of this is lighter than those where pieces are involved; then press it as follows hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken into pieces, they must be held from two sides, whether it is a hand or foot, or with your hands for smaller members, or with two cords, or one cord and your hands; and place the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the fractured bone are separated, you reset all the additions in their places as much as possible, and be careful that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient; and align the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And you can feel well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not right: then straighten it properly, and do not pull too hard, nor press so as to cause inflammation of the abscess and contraction of the limb as those who work on this often cause many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is properly set, instruct the patient well not to move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor in turning, nor in any other way; and ensure that the limb is so secure that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels any pain, it is not properly set, and it must be placed in such a position that it does not feel any pain; and make sure it is positioned correctly so that no curvature comes about when it is restored; and the quality of the fractured limb depends on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs such as arms and thighs: they should be wrapped in soft and fine linen cloths; and for those that are large, such as legs and thighs: it is necessary to wrap them with wide and hard bandages, because the broad bandages embrace the entire large limb evenly, so there is no gap; then tie around light wadding, three or four turns according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little over the entire bandage, then press above the break lightly, so that the break can slightly separate from each other; gradually loosen the bandage bit by bit until you cover most of the healthy area, then take another bandage and start wrapping again on top of the broken area; then tie below the break moderately, neither too tight nor too loose, as we said in the first chapter above; then place wadding made of linen or cloth between the bandages so that everything is even, then secure it all with a broad strip, and finally place your well-made splints if there are no abscesses or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place a soothing, hot abscess poultice upon it, and one that reduces the swelling, and leave it thus for some days; then incise over your needles, and let them be half the width of a finger thick, or from wood used to make clives, or from palm ribs, and arrange them according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the needle placed over the fracture be slightly thicker and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as needed for the limb, whether small or large; then incise over the needles as you did in the first suture, then place a thread above it, just as in the first suture over the break; tighter is better, less so worse; and it must be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and should be made of soft linen; for if the threads are too thick, as I have seen with those who make their sutures from twisted linen cords, this is a great error, because the suture cannot be equal if it is too fine, and there must not be less than two fingers' width between each needle.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is pierced by the points of stars after they are tightened in their places, then place under them lint rolls, or wool rags, so that they do not become infected.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the breaker, and the bone is broken, I will tell the treatment for it hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you should know that it is not appropriate to extract all broken members with nails on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the member is large, it is not appropriate to place nails before five days or seven, or more depending on your certainty of a hot abscess that may occur; and see here the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: which is that you take flour that is kept at the walls of the mill, and mix it abundantly with eggs, and apply this preparation, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the plaster restoring fractures in various conditions, especially for women and small children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to make a plaster for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: take З of abares and styrax and enula and asafoetida and gum arabic and mastic, ana X З.; myrrh and aloes, ana V З.; aleche IX З.; and make powder, and mix with egg white; if the person's constitution is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and hastens the restoration of broken bones, and suits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to make a plaster for twists: take mastic and visnaga, ana X З.; myrrh and aloes, ana IX З.; acacia VI З.; Armenian bole X З., and grind well, and mix with water or egg white, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to make a plaster for joints and bones that have come out of place, and to ease the pain that comes with it, and the wear on the bone, and fractures: take new wool, boil it in grease and oil, and apply it to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess and properly relieves the pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to make a plaster that heals broken bones: take dried mulberry leaves and plantain leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make a plaster for the healing of a broken bone and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take roots of valerian, chamomile, violets, flour of oats, of each one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the member is heated, mix it with moist coriander water, or just water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of making an ointment stronger than the first one, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of valerian, seeds of flax, hawthorn, sweet clover, and pennyroyal, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of each one part; and grind, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that one should not place on the broken limb to restore strength anything but waxed cloth made of wax and oil, and nothing more, and he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says that for restoring a broken limb, dry and slightly warm things should be applied, such as myrrh, aloes, and incense, and similar items, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to make an ointment that is good for injuries and pain: take mutton suet, human hair cuttings, bird feathers, and vervain, in equal parts, and grind them together, then make an ointment with it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then undo it a little while after, and be careful if the patient does not feel any pain or if the bone is not out of place; do not undo it by hand again If pain comes to the area, or itching, without rest or swelling, hurry and undo it, and remove the plaster now; take a light cloth, and sponge from the sea moistened, and dip in water, and lift up the area, until the itching stops, and the pain is eased; then leave the limb to rest for an hour, then put on dry wool soaked in water or rose oil, and tie it down with a nut, until you are sure of no hot abscess; and rest the inflammation of the member, and let the pain go away, then start the thin bandage again, and a little plaster, and do not squeeze as hard as before; and gently until he is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen are all gone from the bone, and you need plaster and linen, then restart it, as you did first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb none of what we have said, do not dislocate it except after III days or IIII or V or VII; and sometimes leave it for XX days, according to what you see, until the bruise subsides, and bring the bones closer together; then restrain it more than before, and fatten its flesh as I said before; and if you see the area dry more than necessary, know that no new tissue can come there; pour it warm water every time you dislocate it, every third day, and loosen the bandage a little; thus by this work stop the formation of new tissue in the limb, and quickly correct what quack doctors do, who reset the limb too soon: that is wrong, and such works are dangerous, and I see no other thing but to leave it and treat it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of fractures, and various figures, and the causes are distinct; for there are fractures made by the impact of a sword, and it breaks all the bone up to the spongy part that is inside the bone, as if it were splitting a shaft or rod; and therefore this kind of fracture is called "haichure.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound from these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded impact, or a split from a stone blow, or falling on a stone, or other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which approaches as far as the membrane that is beneath the bone, or is on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound in the bone as fine as a hair, and the crack is small, and for this reason it is called a "capillary" fracture; and if the wound is made by being hit with a stone, or by falling, or by similar things, and causes a piece of bone to go inward, and the place where it happens resembles how metalworkers form dents when hammering on pots; then the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have in their head soft bones, such as the head of a child; and all these types of fractures result in small pieces being dislodged like splinters; and I will speak about them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all manners of fractures by the depression upon them, and the inquiry with probes, and by the corrupted flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is recognized when, after uncovering the bone, one rubs along it, and the fracture appears clearly black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be cautious of any adverse effects on the patient, and if you see any bad symptoms, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, pallor, intermittent fever, and the eyes protruding and turning red, and other similar conditions in many cases, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming symptoms and hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person comes to you first, and it is in winter, then remove the bone before the fourteenth day from the wound that you may.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone does not become corrupted, and the accidents we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the tissue that covers the brain, then you must proceed as follows: take the head of the injured person and expose the bone in every way possible, and over the area of the wound as deeply as you can. If blood flows when exposing the bone or an abscess occurs, treat it appropriately with whatever is necessary, which means filling the place with cloths soaked in rose oil; then rest the wound until the hot abscess subsides and bleeding stops; then begin to remove around the bone, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method involves cutting closely ahead of the incision, and here is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make the other incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have various incisions of different sizes, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron; and work gently so that you do not injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and protruding, you must pierce around it, thus administering incisions with awls, not piercing beyond the soft part of the skull bone, and it should have a margin or circle above the point so that the tip does not pass through the bone; and you need to have several of them so that each fits in its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have awls for the entire head; and this is the form of the three types of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to pierce around the broken bone is that you place a probe on the bone and turn it until you know the bone is pierced; then move the probe slightly further apart, and do this all around, then with the lancets cut between the perforations of the bone as finely and lightly as we have said, so that you draw out the bone into your hand or any tool you have such as pliers, pincers; and take care not to touch the brain or cerebellum.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, it is necessary to use an instrument that remains with the bone, similar to a lancet, but it must be thicker and finer than other lancets; and if any small bones or scales remain, remove them gently with the instruments; then treat the wound with dressings and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galen said, who was more skilled; and he praises it greatly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone where the fracture is visible, so that when you have uncovered this part, place beneath the head of this lenticle incisor, which has this shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is beveled on two sides, so that the cutting edge faces the bone; then strike with a small mallet, so that you lightly cut around the bone, and take great care of the tissue beneath; if it adheres to the bone, remove it gently, for it can be removed without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate to the skin, and the bone is only cut from above, with small pieces present, then you must smooth over those rough areas, and remove the scales using a fine scraper of which you should have various quantities, to best suit each place according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Start with large scrapers and then use finer ones, and continue this process until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cuts and fine fractures, you must treat them according to their condition; and this is something that cannot be mastered by one who has not dedicated study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the brain is exposed, you should take a piece of linen according to the size of the wound, moisten it in rose oil, and place it over the wound; then take another piece of linen doubled in two or three layers, soak it in wine and rose oil, and put it on top of the first piece of linen; do this as gently as possible so that you do not burden the brain, then cover with another cloth without tightening too much so that it just covers the wound; leave it like this for one or two days until the abscess is calmed, then remove it and apply medicines such as lily root, wheat flour, powdered frankincense, aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder from these substances and place it on the wound, and promptly apply cleansing remedies without irritation; ensure that the wound remains clean, do not leave any ointment behind, nor allow pus to accumulate on the skin covering the brain, for when pus accumulates over the brain's tissue, it can rot and cause great harm to the patient; if something irritating is applied to the brain, cover it with a layer above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, pay attention if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness appears other than from the medicine applied on it, having such efficacy, then you should take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix in one drachma, and apply this to the surface; then treat it according to appropriate methods until he is well.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the skull above are broken, or just one of them, because these are two bones; and the lower one is made of cartilage, and does not break, unless it is forced to bend or twist, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must insert your small rod or probe into the anus, and place the break evenly within your guiding rod, and slightly outside the pouch, until the anus returns to its natural shape; do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the anus, and your rod cannot reach the place, then you must place it evenly at the head of a slightly thickened area.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, then do likewise, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after seven or ten days, when the abscess has subsided, then insert into the head of the anus patches of linen cloth if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you place one side against the other where the fracture is; and let the tents be so thick that they fill the openings of the anus.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some practitioners say that the tents should be lubricated with butter, and changed each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think this is good, but they should be moistened with a preparation of yolk of egg and flour powder; then leave the tent in place until the bone is hard and the cartilage is firm.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes goose feathers are inserted instead of tents, and if there is a fine cloth around them, and the fracture stays in place, and blows pass through them; do as you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose while you are working on them, apply wax or moistened cotton in rose oil, or a piece of myrrh.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no abscesses come to them, apply a plaster behind, made of sesame flour and powdered incense, cooked with some egg white, then place light plugs and do not tie the nose; and if the nasal fracture is small, and it is broken into small pieces, remove them with suitable instruments, then stitch the wound, and treat with substances that heal flesh, and binding, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this purpose; and if there are no wounds inside the nose, cure it with tents, and place strips of cloth, until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured away from its socket, and there is no wound to be seen, and the break is only slightly displaced, and it is not broken into two pieces, but merely disjointed inside, one can easily recognize this.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, you should place your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left mandible, use your right index finger, gently insert it into the fracture from the outside, and support it with the other hand to align it evenly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is displaced in two parts, you must administer an extension to both sides until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth occurs, or fracture, then pull them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then place on the broken mandible wax, and put on two cloths; and place on the cloth a large stick well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width according to the mandible, and tie it securely as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and consume light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then untie it on the third day and then adjust what has changed; and apply a poultice with powder from the mill mixed abundantly with eggs or sesame flour, after removing the wax; and place light wool over the poultice, and if the poultices adhere and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is well; many times he will be well in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if large abscesses come, then treat them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine whether any piece of the bone has been removed; then carefully remove it with appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, then sew the wound if it is large, and apply suitable plasters to it, to promote flesh growth until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The collarbone breaks several times in front of the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three manners: where it is broken and separated into two parts, and there are pieces, and this is the easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is such that when the fracture is without an open wound, you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the collarbone is broken; and the other extends the neck towards the affected part; then equalize the fracture with your hands, so that its form is as it should be, and there be neither appearance nor displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place under the patient's shoulder a round ball of cloth or wool, and make it as thick as necessary; then extend and lift the collarbone, and hold the ball with your hand so that you can equalize the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the clavicle outward because it is deep within, then have the patient lie supine on their back, and place a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder, and push the minister's shoulder down until the bone of the clavicle is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then align the fracture with your hands, and if you find it broken, then it is necessary to cut into it; gently pull apart the pieces, and if the bone cannot join due to any obstacle, cut it with one of the saws you have; but place under the clavicle this instrument, to protect the surface:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it resembles a spoon, and is not bristled, and should be as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and let it have two edges, as you see, one broad, and the other narrow, like the wound you made when you pulled apart the bones; and when you are certain of a hot abscess, close the wound, and if the wound is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, cover the wound with cloths and tents according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses occur, wet the cloth in rose oil and egg yolk and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The treatment of the broken bone, when there is no wound and no incision, is that you place on the bone a plaster made from flour powder and egg white, then put in light bandages, and if needed, place a sphere under the healthy side; then take a very wide bandage about one palm wide, and place a double cloth and the plaster over it; then take a slender stick three fingers wide and long, wrap the bandage around this stick so that the ends hang down; place the stick on the fracture, wrap the bandage around the neck, under both armpits; secure each part tightly, and when you see that the ligature holds the break in place clearly, and the stick does not move from the bone, check it every day, and when the binding loosens, retighten it; have the patient lie on their back, placing a small pillow under the healthy side to lift it up, which will lighten the shoulder fracture by lifting the arm; tie the arm to the neck for twenty days without removing it unless an adverse event occurs; then restart the plaster if needed, and continue to bind and leave as is until it heals; this usually takes about twenty-eight days or less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Rarely does the shoulder break at its widest point or in the middle, and it is only known through palpation; treat it according to the appearance of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form, in all possible ways; then apply powder from the mill with an abundance of egg, and use light bandages, and place a double cloth on top; then place a broad but fine frame over it, slightly wider than the shoulder, and if any part of the frame is pointed at any point on the shoulder, fill that pointed area with linen bandages so that the frame lies evenly; then bind it tightly with a large strip of cloth, firmly enough that the frame does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and each time it loosens, retighten it, and ensure the frame remains in position if it moves out of place, and have the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder will be restored in twenty or twenty-five days, and when this period is complete, release it, and be sure, for it is not a bone that resets easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes and points away from the heart, cut it off, and do as we have said concerning the fracture to ease a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it tilts to the side, causing the patient great pain, and lack of appetite, and thirst, and sometimes vomiting blood, and the movement of the bone fragments can be felt.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies supine on their back, and a cushion is placed between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and align the ribs of both sides with your hands, and carefully make it even in all ways you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply plasters and poultices over a fine layer of salt or another light powder, and wrap it in a cloth, and secure it on the broken bone so that it does not move; then tie it around the back tightly, and bind it firmly, and check every hour the binding, and if it loosens, tighten it again; and if it needs to be untied, for corrosion or itching that comes at the site, or pain or abscess, then hurry and untie it, apply a plaster, and treat what has come in ways of care; then reapply the plaster and bind it firmly until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of the ribs is strong only in their thick parts behind the back, and at the top where they are smooth; and one feels this well upon examination with both hands.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set the fracture evenly as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster cast, and secure it with a splint if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs inclines inward, then the patient feels great pain and pressure, as with pleurisy, because the bone pierces the tissue; it often causes vomiting and spitting up large amounts of blood, which is a grave condition, and even experienced practitioners find it difficult to treat.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push the fracture apart.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this so that shallow abscesses do not occur if they have not already come about.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have occurred, then heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say to apply suction cups to the area, to draw out forcefully, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the suction cups will attract the excesses to the area due to the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say to cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to make the dressing even, then treat it according to the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medication.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the bone piercing the skin, and there is doubt in the patient's mind, it is necessary to cut along the side of the broken rib, and place a tool underneath to protect the surface; then one must cut the bone lightly, and then suture the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat with plasters until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if small abscesses come, place strips moistened in rose oil over them; and treat the area as needed for an abscess, and let the patient lie on their side where it is necessary, until they are healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck (or collarbone)
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a fracture of the neck bones, and it can happen that they bend; and similarly with the spine.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if they will recover or not, observe if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when you pinch and prick them, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the patient can be treated, if proper care is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine, and you wish to know if they will recover or not, observe if the feet are weakened, and if there are symptoms like those in the hands, and on the back there is bloating and involuntary evacuation; and when one lifts them onto their belly, there is involuntary evacuation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is fatal: do not attempt to treat it.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not occur, then the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you should treat it if there is a hot abscess, apply rose oil or boiled egg oil until it subsides; then place one of the soothing and drying plasters on it, and bandage it with a cloth, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not let him sleep on the part where he feels pain, until he is well.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone breaks, it must be treated by the chest; remove the bone, then sew together the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat it with an ointment that promotes flesh growth until it heals; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the shoulder," place your thumb from your left hand there, and make it equal to the other side as best you can, then apply the plaster and bandage if necessary; then bind it tightly, and if there are any loose bones, cut them away and remove them, treating the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it does happen, there is usually only a slight reduction at the head; and it fractures along its length, and inclines inwardly, causing pain to the patient in the affected area, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand upon it, so that you are above the fracture; and you ascertain where the break is and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the head, then set it equal so that it has a natural appearance.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is along its length, where it inclines inwardly, then have the patient lie on their belly, so that you can prepare the restoration of that fracture.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, apply the plaster, then place a stick of wood or horn on top, and secure the bandage so that it does not move; and cover the area under the ribs, until the flesh is level.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if hot abscesses appear, do not touch them until the hot abscesses are calmed, and apply what we have said before; then return to the restoration process, and bind it as necessary, if there is no bad outcome; this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the collarbone and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two methods: one of which is that you take a staff full of moistened material, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two heads with two ropes, and lift them up, and seat the patient on a chair; then place the broken arm on the staff, until it reaches the elbow, and have some curvature in the middle of the staff, then lift it up with some heavy object or let the assistant pull down from below; then position the splint equal to both hands, so that the splint returns as needed.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you lift the patient onto his back, and tie the hand to his neck, then instruct two assistants that one pull that which is above the splint towards both hands, and the other pull from below along the entire length of the bandage, each extending at their own part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you wish for the extraction to be stronger, then loosen the ligament below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the muscles on their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the top of the shoulder, then you should place one ligament under the armpit, and another towards the side, below the fracture; and similarly, if the fracture is towards the side, then you should lightly place a ligament without labor until the fracture is level on both sides, and above the side; then make the fracture even as it should be, and press it firmly, unless abscesses occur.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses occur, then do not press them until the seventh day, and place linen soaked in warm rose oil on it until the abscess is calmed; then press it, and the way to press it is that you apply a plaster on the fracture, then bring the arm up to the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest; and put the bandage on, and press around the shoulder and the arm so that the arm is in its proper place, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is displaced.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and place one splint above the fracture wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint a space of two fingers, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three finger-widths on each side; then strain upon the splints as I said at the beginning of the chapter about the fracture, more strongly and less in spreading apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the placement of the splints and the bandaging as we have said, when you restore the fractured limb, and you fear a hot abscess, leave it tied until the seventh day, as we have said; then check the binding every three days to ensure that itching or swelling does not occur at the site where healing cannot take place because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is adjusted as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident occurs, do not attempt to dislocate it sooner than after three days or more, and have the patient sleep on their back, with their hands on their stomach; place under the shoulder one cushion filled evenly with wool, and check every hour of day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move or loosen the ligaments; adjust it by the power of medicine, and give them the food we mentioned earlier, in such a way that the food is initially very light; and when they begin to recover, gradually increase the quantity.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset over forty days in total; then they must be dislocated and administered baths and medicinal ointments to heal the area.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is tight and enclosed, then wait one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "fascicles," of which one is small, and it is the one that lies near the elbow; and the other is large, and it is the one that is below, toward the little finger. Perhaps only the larger fascicle is broken, or perhaps the smaller one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.
