When the smaller fascicle is broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing is quick; and when the larger one is broken, the healing is difficult, and more troublesome than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is merely broken, then it should be gently stretched out and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bone that is broken, then it should be pulled more firmly; and lay him on a cushion, and elevate his hand higher than the others, and the small one lower than the other two, and let the patient lie crossed over himself, with the cushion in front of him raised so that the patient feels no labor; then extend the assistant's arm to the part below at his hand, or at the joint, and another assistant should do the same from above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the bones evenly, according to their natural form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there are fragments of the break, place each in its proper place, and if any fragment pricks the heart and you cannot restore it to its place, cut it away as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the treatment of wounds, I have spoken in a separate chapter; then take that treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration abscesses occur, apply a strip of plaster made from rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard or too soft; and place this strip carefully, until the small abscesses are alleviated.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the wax and apply the plaster made from powder of the mill with plenty of egg, then place the bandages, and ensure that the bandage over the wound is somewhat thicker, and a bit wider than the others; and note that there should be six bandages on the arm in various positions: whether the wound is on one bone or two; hold it tighter over the wound than elsewhere, and gradually less so as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and ensure that the cloths over the wound are soft and moist, not hard or rough; and let the thread from which they are made be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have stated.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And examine the limb and its joint after several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then it is necessary to rinse the limb with hot water until the itch subsides; and allow the limb to rest without pressure.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then restart the compression, and if the joint is weakened and the bone dislocated, and similar issues, address them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And be careful if the swelling cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you should loosen it a bit, and leave it like this for several days until the swelling moves there, and then compress it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the patient, then do not dislocate until twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	When it is around the neck area, then he can put his hands on his neck, and let his necks be equal, and beware of movement and disturbance, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and the temperaments of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and the thumb there are few fractures, and it mostly comes to being a sprain many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or sprained, it is necessary that the patient sits with crossed legs and sits straight in front of them evenly; then place his hand on an extended cloth, and the practitioner should extend the broken bones and align them properly until they are well joined; then apply a plaster and bandages, unless abscesses appear, then place a splint according to the size of the area; and wrap it with one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the middle of the palm at the base of the fingers, make a ball of cloth, and instruct the patient to bind it to his fractured palm; then bind it with a long strip of cloth, and let the stick under the hand be as wide as the palm of the hand, and bind it tightly, as is appropriate.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is towards the side, then you must place a stick on top and another underneath the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it tightly around the hand, and secure the binding between the two sticks.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture affects one of the fingers, whether it is a thumb, set it equal as appropriate; bind it with the palm, and if you wish place a small straight stick to elevate the fractured finger so that it does not move; and if the fracture is in any other fingers such as the index or another, set them equally and bind them together with the healthy adjacent finger; or hold all of them together in whichever way provides better support, or place a stick under them as you would for a thumb; be careful during restoration and treatment of hot abscesses, and assist those who come to you as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh bone
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and this can be seen when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is done by binding one bandage above the break and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their back, then each assistant extends their bandage equally on either side; this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then one bandage should be towards the groin, and the other bandages below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the knee, then the bandage should be near the knee, and the extension downward; then place the bone evenly with both hands, as per its natural shape, and then apply a plaster, and bind it, unless abscesses appear.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside before returning to your work and treatment; the procedure is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the fracture a bandage doubled in two or three layers, and remove any excess; then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the thigh, and insert one long thread between the thigh and the leg near the knee, with the top of the thread above; then wrap the leg and thigh with the bandage, then place splints on the fracture, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and thigh with soft cloth to ensure even compression, then begin to tie firmly three or four turns around the fracture; and as you go further from the fracture, it should be less tight; then join the two threads that you inserted between the leg and thigh, and tie three splints above them, then rejoin below at the top of the thread until you reach near the foot; tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, so that no abscess or swelling or similar occurs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, loosen it as we have said many times before; and if there are pieces of bone that hurt, they must be removed if possible; and if not possible, the area should be cut open and treated accordingly until he is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken in such a way that rods are inserted, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, the patient does not suffer when the restoration is done this way.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in 21 days, or a few less or more, according to the differences in temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the kneecap passage
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee there is often a crack, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is merely a crack, or a small gap, and it results in an injury, and one feels the pain, and this people feel well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to make equal those which are short at its sides, until they are assembled as much as possible; then apply a plaster, and if necessary place a round splint, and secure it properly; then attend to all the measures we have described for other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar conditions; provide each case with what is appropriate, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by its proper name "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and it happens similarly to all kinds of fractures as they occur in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is equally like that of the arm, and the work is the same. And if both bones are broken together, then turn the leg from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bone is broken, then turn it forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, then there is great pain, and it can be seen clearly; and turn it from below.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then administer an extension, and place it evenly, and bind the splints equally; however, if the fracture is severe, and there are multiple pieces, the extension should be smaller and gentler; and proceed according to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of wood that wrap around the leg from both sides, and let them extend from the knee to below; then envelop it with two layers of bandages above and below, and tie it in the middle as well; at this point, the leg cannot turn to the right or left, and thus is secure; some apply a plaster along the length of the leg, and if made of wood, they place it on the leg to prevent movement, and properly done for fractures where there is an open wound; move the leg each day to check for any abscess or other accident; treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the foot bones
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but at the foot bones there sometimes occurs a fracture and in both heels, and there happens weakness that cracks in many conditions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it happens that the foot bones are fractured, and you see these bones protrude one over the other, place the patient's foot on the ground as if he wanted to walk, then put your foot on his where the bones are raised, and press them until they return to their places; then apply a plaster and bandages, and under the sole of the foot place a small board filled with two handfuls, then bind it tightly to the foot after wrapping it in cloths, and other things you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones even, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two are broken, restore them as we have said for the two of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the leg, and it should be a bit wider, then put under the foot the board that I mentioned, and secure it firmly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, place on each one a splint according to its size, wrapped in one piece of linen cloth, and bind the board under the foot; and let them be at the top of the board away from the bottom of the foot so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said to other fractures; and treat each case as is appropriate.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's urethra is fractured, have her sit with her legs spread, then lean her towards the part of the back; and hold her from behind. Then fill the area around the urethra of the patient with cotton, and place in it as much wool as a fist holds; then help the woman stand up, and lift her back little by little, until the cotton reaches the entrance of the urethra, and return the bone along with the wool. When she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has done so, put it back in again; do this for seven days or around that time: the fracture will be restored. If you wish, take a sheep's bladder and tie it at the opening with a tube, then pour all of the bladder into the urethra; blow strongly through the tube until the bladder is full inside: this will help restore the fracture. Then fill it again with cotton and leave it like that for some days, until she is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the thumb of a man is broken, or of a woman, restore it as we have said regarding the thigh bone; and these nearby fractures are not hidden from one who applies his study and use to them, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture signifies in several ways the proper way of restoration: understand then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the shaft, when it is broken, take a goose neck and insert the shaft into it; then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days or until healed, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, to be treated immediately, so that the treatments we have mentioned bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then apply vitriol to constrict it, if you have nothing else, and then resume restoring the fracture at the same hour, or on that day, unless abscesses appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses appear, then leave the restoration until a new day, until the abscesses are calmed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause an evil occurrence.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on the exposed chest, then it is necessary to set it gently by hand with slight traction.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if you do not have the means to extend it equally with your hands, then use this instrument made of iron, which is seven or eight inches long, and its width corresponds to the size of the wound; and for this, it is necessary that the physician has three or four such instruments, according to what is needed for each fracture treatment; let it be smooth and a bit thick, so that it does not bend under compression on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp in front, and thicker from the middle forward, as follows:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", for which the curved head must be placed on top of the visible bone; and push it at once until it returns and they are equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone until the instrument has enough hold.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, either an incisor or saw, to your ability; then remove what remains in the bone of hardness and small fragments.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you place it in its proper position, then moisten the flap with black styptic wine and properly clean if it is dirty; do not put cerate or anything else on the wound that has oil, as it may cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer splints after you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover only around the edges according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the dressing does not compress the fracture; and many times foolish physicians have done this and caused death or corrosion to the patient; and let the bindings be looser and lower than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that harm may come as we have said, and you find pain in the area, then splints must not be placed on it; but wrap around, instead of splints, hard cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that pus is forming in the wound, remove what you have placed over it entirely, and apply an ointment healing wounds, such as tetrafarmacos ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be prepared in such a way that the pus flows downward gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if several days pass and it cannot heal but continues to pus, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must probe the wound with a probe, and remove all these loose pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to that place, or another manner of corruption, then it is necessary for you to treat it, according to what he says in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar cases involving large limbs, do not attempt to remove it, for many times this leads to death, but leave it until it becomes gangrenous; perhaps it will fall off after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come upon the joints
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see this after the injury, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a terrible sight to see the figure of the limb; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then when the nose is fresh: if the administrator applies astringent medicines such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others, choose any of these or all together, and cook them with stiptic wine or with plenty of egg white or with alum; then place it on the nose in bandages, press tightly, and do not loosen for several days; after that remove it and start another, until the swelling is gone; or you can press on a piece of lead properly made; for the property of lead is to take away all the swellings above the members; and if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, then it must be removed, so cut off the surface, revealing the excess; or have it shaved by someone, until it is gone, and heal as long as necessary.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb which is weak after recovery
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and the limb remains weak and delicate afterwards, this happens for many reasons: one reason being that it was bound too tightly, and not as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, preventing nourishment from reaching the limb; or due to excessive washing; or because of too great movements at the wrong time; or because they have little blood in their body, so they are weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat and make the body soft, until the blood is multiplied within him; then administer baths and give joy and rest; then apply pitch to the limb so that the pitch attracts abundant nourishment, and rinse it often with cold water, until the nourishment flows into the limb; and let it regain its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	from the limb after the healthiness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone broken openly, and the form of the limb is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe those fools who say one must break the limb anew, and many foolish doctors have done this in our land; and such work is blamed, and great harm comes from it, and perhaps death; nonetheless, if the nerves and tendons are fresh, they should be soaked in hot water, or herbs that soften should be boiled, such as leaves of mullein, roots, and hellebore, and similar things; and I make a softening ointment, as well-made as electuary, and you take the muscilaginous paste of mullein, and mix it with fat of quince or oil of cumin, and apply an ointment on top; or you take fatty figs, and crush them with flaxseed meal, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the knot is removed to rub continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be movement of the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuous condition is inflamed and hardened, like a stone, and needs to be removed with iron, then it must be cut down to the bone with a subtle and gentle incision; and apply caution and careful study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to anyone, one must now reset it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the area swells, and by chance it may be reset with difficulty to its place; therefore, it is not fitting that one should move it while it is swollen: many times this causes spasms and other pains. However, when this happens, have the patient bled, then leave him until the abscess is abated; then wash the limb with warm water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each member as the cure will come to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have organized the chapters on dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It rarely happens that the mandibles are dislocated on both sides, and the dislocations of both are according to two manners: where they are slightly removed from their places, and softened a little; or where they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the worse side, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so that it cannot hold it, nor can it close its mouth, and envelops its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns on its own in many cases.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and thorough, then you must reset it quickly, without delay; and in such a manner that the minister holds the head of the patient, and places his fingers into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is from both sides; and the other hand should be behind, to keep them even; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the physician should place it evenly, so that it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to reset, especially if they are both mandibles together, soak them in warm water and oil until you can gently reset them; do not delay in resetting them, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reset evenly, and the patient's mouth needs to remain closed for softening, place cloths soaked in cerate made of rose oil and wax on it, then bind it gently with soft bands; let the patient sleep on their back, with his head resting between two cushions so that he does not move it left or right, nor tries to chew, but eats light food until the pain is gone and the mandibles are healed; then eat what he wishes lightly, without trying to open the mouth for eating or drinking until the mandible is well set and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be reset properly in one hour, and are not returned to their places, it leads to habitual fevers, and by chance there may be diarrhea, and by chance vomiting of bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then you know it is a prognosis of death; and many times the person who experiences it dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	by force
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The dislocation cannot be corrected from the side within the continuity of the ribs and the hip, and it is sometimes dislocated outward, which one can feel.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies supine on their back, and extends their arms; then press the area firmly with your palm, and it will return; then apply the plaster and bandage, and secure it; and the head which is towards the side cannot be dislocated again; if possible not, and if it does dislocate sometimes, reset it to its place as we have said; then apply the plaster and bandage, and secure it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; and similarly, the shoulder joint that has been separated from its place is restored in this manner.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated according to three manners: one of which is that it dislocates at the part near the socket on the inner side; and the second is at the part of the humerus; and sometimes it dislocates above, but this rarely happens; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor within for the nerves; and more often it dislocates below towards the socket, especially in those who have little flesh, because it tends to happen quickly to them; to those who have enough flesh, it occurs with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that they suffer a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they believe that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	You must then test it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	Dislocation is recognized when it moves towards the socket, and there is a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear distinction between them; and you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, below the socket as if it were an eye; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose or move in any way; and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not concealed, for you will feel it clearly upon palpation; and this type of dislocation is not easily reduced when it is fresh, or if a child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The method is that the practitioner lifts the patient's hand upwards, then places their fingers below the socket, and raises the joint forcefully to its place; and the practitioner lifts the arm, and extends it upwards, then brings it down; it will quickly return.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said within a few days, the patient should be bathed in hot water; and apply a soft and soothing remedy, such as a decoction of hellebore, fenugreek, and honey-suckle in water, and then rub the patient on his back; place under the bench a cushion of wool even, not too soft nor too hard, then put your heel on the cushion, lift the head of the patient vigorously, and pull the arm of the patient; another attendant should hold the head of the patient so that it does not move down; this shoulder returns now completely, and if you wish to reset it according to this method: have a man present who is larger than the patient; let him stand by the side of the patient, put his shoulder under the bench of the patient, lift the bench up, so that the patient hangs on the rope; another attendant should pull the arm of the patient downward toward the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, something heavy may be placed with him, and now the dislocation returns.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is reset in another way as well: place a long stake in the ground, which should be as thick as a pistol, neither too big nor too thin; then position it under the patient, but cover it with cloths so that the skin does not touch directly; let the patient lean against this stake; then extend his arm on the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; if it does not want to return despite all these things we have said, do this cure: take a stake two arms long and four thumbs wide, which has a blunt end for insertion under the armpit, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then bind the head of the body with a cloth so that the body does not hurt the patient, then place it under the seat of the patient; and stretch his arm on the long staff, and bind the shoulder to the staff, and the hand at the top of the staff, then put the arm on one side of a wide ladder, and let the hand hang down, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will now come back into place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, however that may be, you must put under the seat a pad of even linen, then apply a poultice prepared with ground powder, with incense and egg yolk mixture all over the shoulder and around it, then stretch out underneath the seat gradually, and wrap the bandage over the poultice, and hug the hand to the neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he fasts a little, until the limb is strengthened, for it will heal more quickly; and then eat more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is dislocated due to moisture that has come to it, or for another reason, then you must administer cauterizations with three holes as described before in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and after seven days it still does not hold, and the arm cannot be raised, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut, stretched, or weakened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation towards the hip, and the breasts, or behind, is done by pushing and stretching with the hands, and another assistant helps in other places; and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the limb becomes stiff and slow in movement, the patient should take many baths until the stiffness is relieved, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the elbow
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the elbow is dislocated by points and returns to them; and if it is dislocated from all sides, especially front and back, and the dislocation is not remedied, as it can be seen and felt clearly; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased part with the healthy part, then you can see clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is displaced, and he cannot bend his arm or touch his shoulder properly.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it as if for deep abscesses that may occur there, because if deep abscesses were to occur, they would be difficult to treat; and perhaps it cannot be completely reset when it is at the back; this condition is worse than other dislocations, causes greater pain, and may lead to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is as follows: when it can be reset, you should extend his hand with your two hands; and his arm should be spread out, and place your hands around the joint, above and below, and bring the joint back to its proper place at the base of his palm.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is to the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and feel from the root of the palm the knife that is out of place.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; and when two ministers extend the arm, and hold it with two ministers so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth around it; and when the joint is brought back to the wrist, apply some ointment to soften the joint, then insert the joint firmly until it returns; and once it is in place, put on dry emplastrum with egg yolk, and bind it tightly, and attach the arm to the neck of the patient, and leave it for several days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, undo the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, repeat the plaster and the bandage, and leave it thus for several days until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels stiffness after the joint is returned, and it moves, bathe and rub gently, and press until it is relieved; or place a sheep's fat pelt on the joint, then leave it for one day and night, then remove it, and let him enter the bath; when he sweats, gently rub the joint with something tempered, then put the pelt back on, and let him enter the bath again; do this two or three times until he is well; if you wish, place moistened birch bark heated with butter over it, and press it on; thus will it return to its proper condition.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is easy to reset, more so than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place quickly, in the same hour that it is dislocated, before swelling occurs or an abscess develops.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the method of resetting it is that you place the injured hand on a table, and the assistant extends the hand, and the healer places their palm equally over the appearance of the joint, pressing until it returns to its proper position. Always, you must check if it is in the right place; then have the patient place the back of their hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, the patient should place the back of his hand on the table, and the physician should place his hand upon that part of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is well. If not, apply emplaisters to soothe the abscesses and leave them without restarting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back after several days, the joint remains dislocated. And it does no harm to the patient other than when the hand is swollen, and he cannot grasp anything at all: then you know that the nerves or arteries are severed; there is no other cause but to cauterize near the case, and perhaps nothing else may help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when it is in place, apply the plaster we have mentioned, then press and leave it for five days, then unbind and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well and there is some stiffness, moisten it with warm water, and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated in each direction, sometimes on the back or palm; then the finger is bent, and the dislocation pushed into place until it returns, then support the head of the finger and pull it towards the part where it is dislocated; leave it for two days, and then make it equal on that day; bind it as we have said, and unbind it daily, and move it, and tie it again; do this often, until it becomes tight, and do exactly the same if it is dislocated on the palm of the hand, and do as you did before, until it heals; and do likewise when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the back ridge
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the dislocation of the back or neck is reset, if there are many resets, there is no cure, for death quickly follows the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that involuntary movements occur, and they cannot be held, and sometimes certain limbs become weakened, either both thighs or both arms or one. And many times the dislocation moves to four parts; when it moves to the back, it is called "gilbositez": the treatment is to check if the gilbositez came from childhood: there is no cure or immediate healing then.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And for those who fall or are struck or similar things, the ancient methods of treatment were described with great words, which bring little benefit in all cases; but I have abbreviated them according to my understanding, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the case of flatfoot pain at the front foot, there is no remedy or cure; and likewise with that which comes directly on both sides, and cannot be cured except by the one properly for the back, as I said; and it should be that the patient lies stretched out on his face in an equal place, and has something to support him from underneath so he does not hurt himself; then put a torch at the head in the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a rope under the armpits of the patient, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two assistants hold the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two torches; and they should be well secured, the torch as we have said, and the physician places his palms on the spine firmly, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this cure, take a board three arms long, and place it under the wall, and have the patient lie on their side, then put the end of the board under the wall, then place the middle of the board over the spine; and have the patient's feet rest on the other end of the board, and press well until it returns to its place; and if you wish, do it with a lever that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And when you drive two torches at the head of the patient with one arm's length, and near the feet two others, there should be a palm's distance between each torch above and below; and in each torch there is one hole where the lever can turn, and they must be firmly fixed in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of torches there should be a turning torch upon which the ropes turn, and at each turning torch there are two small torches of a palm's length to turn the lever; then tie one rope among the blocks to the lever towards the head, and the other rope near the feet to the other lever, and each attendant turns their own lever for all the rope, and the master places the spine level as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, place on a desiccative poultice with plenty of egg, and then the bandages, and then the stick from a tablet three fingers long, to cover the area of the gibbosity and the part of the vertebra that is healthy, then the juice of a plant, as we have said, and use gentle nursing until he is well; and if anything comes at the end of the healing process, one must administer softening and soothing medicines, with the stick that we mentioned above; and sometimes there is administered a piece of lead, and sometimes an appearance occurs in the last vertebra of the back, and it is thought to be dislocation; and this bone shows its nature, for which one should not presume: by chance it could bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that at the joints of the hip and the shoulder, only dislocations occur, not like other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: inward and outward, and front and back; and more inward than elsewhere, and slightly dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the recognition of an inward dislocation is that when the affected leg is joined with the healthy one, it appears longer, and the patient's knee appears more bent than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee to the fire; and the area near it is swollen with abscesses and hot, because the thigh bone comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the signs of him who is coming to faint are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him who is coming before are such that he straightens his leg according to the fulfillment; nonetheless, he does not double his knee without pain, and if one wants to make him go forward, he cannot advance, and he retains his urine, and his ankle swells, and when he walks, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who is coming behind are such that he cannot extend his knee or bend it, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh is in a position below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedy for this resemblance of dislocation is that you observe whether the dislocation is ancient, and it remains according to its condition, with no treatment needed; and there should be no presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is one of the four types of dislocations, hurry to return the joint, and move it inward and outward, and rotate it right and left; perhaps it will return, and there is no need for other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare one minister to firmly extend the leg with two hands, or tie it above the knee; and another minister places his hand on top such that he pushes his hands under the patient's buttocks, then tightens them into a single bandage on the thigh; and another holds the head of the bandage; and they all pull upwards and downwards at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground in one motion, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to the four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then you must treat it according to its likeness. When the dislocation is in the thigh, you should lift the patient onto their healthy side, then place a bandage at the root of the injured thigh and below the joint; then stretch the bandage upwards towards the joint and towards the muscles; take another assistant by the arms and have them embrace the large part of the injured thigh and stretch it out forcefully: it will now return to its place; and this type of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot secure it in the manner we have described, then bind the patient's two feet together with a strong bandage below the heels and above the knees; let the injured leg be stretched out two palms longer than the other; then suspend the patient from the top of a pole so that he is two arm lengths off the ground; then instruct one assistant to embrace the upper part of the thigh, while another suspends himself with the patient, embracing the thigh firmly, for now the joint will return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is out of place, let the patient lie down, as we have said about one who has gout, and bind a linen strip tightly around the affected leg, and similarly on the foot; then place two torches, one at the head and another at the feet, then insert a torch between the thighs of the patient in its proper form; and let wet cloths be placed around it so that it does not burn the patient, then each assistant extend towards him, and the physician places his hand equally on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on the table and press as we have said in the case of gout, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to quickly extend the affected leg as I have said; and let the healers place their effort to be on top of the affected joint, then press with the other hand, and stretch downwards towards the knee.
