Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is behind, one should not extend the affected leg downwards nor lift it up, but rather it must be as if the hip were dislocated backwards, as we have described in the position on the two hips; and let him lie on his back, with the limb stretched out as we said before, and press on the joint towards the table; and it is ready when the patient extends his legs equally; then join the thighs together, apply the plaster, and bind them tightly so that the hip does not move; rest for three or four days, then unbind and reapply the plaster; if you see that they are equal again, bind them as before and leave them for three days; then unbind him, and make him walk gently until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: namely, inward and outward, and backward; it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the thigh, and if it does not rest on the thigh, then you know it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such cases is as follows: make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his chest, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your hands, then bend the two sides of the knee firmly; and another assistant extends his foot so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he holds his leg lightly at the thigh; and apply a plaster over it, and bandage the leg tightly to the thigh, and tie them together firmly for three or four days, then release him; and do not let the patient work on walking until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not properly aligned, apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the thigh, until it is healthy
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes bruised, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it feels soft in the area where it is dislocated: the reduction is easy, and one should gently extend it with their hands when it is only bruised.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you should have the patient sit straight, and hold them firmly by the leg above the ankle; then pull the foot towards yourself with your right hand, and then twice with the left hand, then extend it upwards, and forcefully push the foot upwards; do this twice as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, repeat the work, for it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, lie the patient on their back on the ground, and firmly fix a board between their thighs, securing cloths around them so they do not move; then hold the leg with one assistant by the thigh, and another pulls the foot with hands or a strap tied to the ankle bone; then extend both assistants equally, and the board should be steady between the patient's thighs to keep the patient still when extending; then place the dislocation equally in your hands, and another assistant holds the healthy leg from behind, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is at the right time, place the plaster and wads on it, then bind it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, taking care that the ligature does not squeeze the nerves behind the ankle; then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandage becomes loose, tighten it again; then loosen it on the third day or fourth, and forbid the patient from walking for four days; and if he walks before this time is up, there is no certainty that he will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if painful swellings occur, you must alleviate them as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both are dislocated, they must be gently extended without effort, and this is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any knot of the back of the foot, you must make the patient sit on a flat place or on a straight table, and put your foot under what appears to be those joints, then press with your foot firmly until it returns; and when they are even, and nothing appears amiss, place a board under the sole of the foot that is two fists wide, then stretch it firmly, and leave it for three days, then release it; and let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and you wish to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in treatment if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for long, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and slow, not bold; and use at first things soothing for heat sores, and leave the patient in God's hands if there is no hope of health; and when there is hope, then now put the limb back to its place as with hot abscesses; and when the member is in place, administer soothing things for heat sores, and treat the wound as it should be done with drying ointments; and if along with dislocation there is a fracture and small bones displaced, remove them and do what we have said in simple diseases; and guard against entering the path of fear according to what I have said, for this grants you more according to your Creator, and for the wisdom of your skill and body.
Amen	So be it
